Then the Blessed One thought: 'What if I were to leave intact the skin, and hide, and flesh, and ligaments, and bones,
 
 <!------------------------page 120------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_120"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 120</font></a>
 
 and marrow of this Nâga; but were to conquer the fire, which he will send forth, by my fire.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="15:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. And the Blessed One effected the appropriate exercise of miraculous power and sent forth a cloud of smoke. Then the Nâga, who could not master his rage<a name="page_120_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_120_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, sent forth flames. And the Blessed One, converting his body into fire<a name="page_120_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_120_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>, sent forth flames. When they both shone forth with their flames, the fire room looked as if it were burning and blazing, as if it were all in flames. And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas, surrounding the fire room, said: 'Truly, the countenance of the great Sama<i>n</i>a is beautiful, but the Nâga will do harm to him<a name="page_120_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_120_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a>.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="15:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. That night having elapsed, the Blessed One, leaving intact the skin and hide and flesh and ligaments and bones and marrow of that Nâga, and conquering the Nâga's fire by his fire, threw him into his alms-bowl, and showed him to the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa (saying), 'Here you see the Nâga, Kassapa; his fire has been conquered by my fire.' Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa thought: 'Truly the great Sama<i>n</i>a possesses high magical powers and great faculties, in that he is able to conquer by his fire the fire of that savage Nâga king, who is possessed of magical power, that dreadfully venomous serpent. He is not, however, holy (arahâ) as I am.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="15:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font><a name="page_120_fr_4"></a><a href="#page_120_note_4"><sup><small>4</small></sup></a>. Near the Nera<i>ñg</i>arâ river the Blessed One
 
 <!------------------------page 121------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_121"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 121</font></a>
 
 said to the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa: 'If it is not disagreeable to you, Kassapa, let me dwell this moonlight night in your fire room.'</p>
 
 <p>   'It is not disagreeable to me, great Sama<i>n</i>a, but in your own behalf I warn you off. There is a savage Snake king there possessed of magical power, a dreadfully venomous serpent; let him do no harm to you.'</p>
 
 <p>   'He is not likely to do any harm to me; pray, Kassapa, allow me a place in your fire room.'</p>
 
 <p>   When he saw that Kassapa had given his permission, fearlessly He, who had overcome all fear, entered. When the chief of Serpents saw that the Sage had entered, he became irritated, and sent forth a cloud of smoke. Then the chief of men<a name="page_121_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_121_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, joyful and unperplexed, also sent forth a cloud of smoke. Unable to master his rage, the chief of Serpents sent forth flames like a burning fire. Then the chief of men<a name="page_121_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_121_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, the perfect master of the element of fire, also sent forth flames. When they shone forth both with their flames, the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas looked at the fire room (saying), 'Truly the countenance of the great Sama<i>n</i>a is beautiful, but the Nâga will do harm to him.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="15:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. And when that night had elapsed, the flames of the Nâga were extinguished, but the various-coloured flames of Him who is possessed of magical powers remained. Dark blue and red, light red, yellow, and crystal-coloured flames of various colours
 
 <!------------------------page 122------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_122"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 122</font></a>
 
 appeared on the A<u>n</u>girasa's<a name="page_122_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_122_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> body. Having put the chief of Serpents into his alms-bowl, he showed him to the Brâhma<i>n</i>a (saying), 'Here you see the Nâga, Kassapa; his fire has been conquered by my fire.'</p>
 
 <p>   And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa, having conceived an affection for the Blessed One in consequence of this wonder, said to the Blessed One: 'Stay with me, great Sama<i>n</i>a, I will daily provide you with food.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the first Wonder.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 16======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="16"></a><font color="GREEN">16</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="16:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. And the Blessed One resided in a certain grove near the hermitage of the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa. And on a beautiful night the four Mahârâ<i>g</i>as<a name="page_122_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_122_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>, filling the whole grove with light by the brilliancy of their complexion, went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him and respectfully saluted the Blessed One, they stood in the four directions like great firebrands.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="16:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. And when that night had elapsed, the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him, he said to the Blessed One: 'It is time, great Sama<i>n</i>a, the meal is ready. Who were they, great Sama<i>n</i>a, who came, this beautiful night, filling the whole grove with light by the brilliancy of their complexion, to
 
 <!------------------------page 123------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_123"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 123</font></a>
 
 the place where you were, and having approached you and respectfully saluted you, stood in the four directions like great firebrands?'</p>
 
 <p>   'They were the four Mahârâ<i>g</i>as, Kassapa, who came to me in order to hearmy preaching.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa thought: 'Truly the great Sama<i>n</i>a possesses high magical powers and great faculties, since even the four Mahârâ<i>g</i>as come to hear his preaching. He is not, however, holy like me.'</p>
 
 <p>   And the Blessed One ate the food offered by the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa, and continued to stay in that same grove.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the second Wonder.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 17======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="17"></a><font color="GREEN">17</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="17:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. And on a beautiful night Sakka (Sakra or Indra) the king of the devas, filling the whole grove with light by the brilliancy of his complexion, went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him and respectfully saluted the Blessed One, he stood near him like a great firebrand, surpassing in beauty and brilliancy the splendour of the former appearances.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="17:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. And when that night had elapsed (&amp;c., as in chap. 16. 2).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the third Wonder.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 124------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_124"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 124</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 18======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="18"></a><font color="GREEN">18</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   And on a beautiful night Brahmâ Sahampati (&amp;c., as in chap. 17).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the fourth Wonder.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 19======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="19"></a><font color="GREEN">19</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="19:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time a great sacrifice which the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa used to celebrate was approaching, and all the people of A<u>n</u>ga and Magadha wished to go to that sacrifice carrying abundant food, both hard and soft. Now the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa thought: 'Presently my great sacrifice is approaching, and all the people of A<u>n</u>ga and Magadha will come and bring with them abundant food, both hard and soft. If the great Sama<i>n</i>a should perform a wonder before that great assembly, gain and honour would increase to the great Sama<i>n</i>a, and my gain and honour would diminish. Well, the great Sama<i>n</i>a shall not appear here to-morrow.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="19:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then the Blessed One, understanding by the power of his mind this reflection which had arisen in the mind of the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa, went to Uttara Kuru; having begged alms there, he took the food (he had received) to the Anotatta lake<a name="page_124_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_124_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>; there he took his meal and rested during the heat of the day at the same place.</p>
 
 <p>   And when the night had elapsed, the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him, he said to the
 
 <!------------------------page 125------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_125"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 125</font></a>
 
 Blessed One: 'It is time, great Sama<i>n</i>a, the meal is ready. Why did you not come yesterday, great Sama<i>n</i>a? We have thought of you: "Why does the great Sama<i>n</i>a not come?" and your portions of food, both hard and soft, were served up for you.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="19:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. (Buddha replied): 'Did you not think, Kassapa: "Presently my great sacrifice (&amp;c., as above down to:). Well, the great Sama<i>n</i>a shall not appear here tomorrow?"</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="19:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. 'Now I understood, Kassapa, by the power of my mind this reflection which had arisen in your mind, and I went to Uttara Kuru; having begged alms there, I took the food to the Anotatta lake; there I took my meal and rested during the heat of the day at the same place.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa thought: 'Truly the great Sama<i>n</i>a possesses high magical powers and great faculties, since he is able to understand by the power of his mind the thoughts of other people. He is not, however, holy like fie.' And the Blessed One ate (&amp;c., as in chap. 16, 2).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the fifth Wonder.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 20======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="20"></a><font color="GREEN">20</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the Blessed One had rags taken from a dust heap (of which he was going to make himiself a dress). Now the Blessed One thought: 'Where shall I wash these rags?' Then Sakka the king of the devas, understanding in his mind the thought which had arisen in the mind of the Blessed One, dug a tank with his own hand, 
 
 <!------------------------page 126------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_126"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 126</font></a>
 
 and said to the Blessed One: 'Lord, might the Blessed One wash the rags here.'</p>
 
 <p>   And the Blessed One thought: 'What shall I rub the rags upon?' Then Sakka the king of the devas, understanding, &amp;c., put there a great stone and said: 'Lord, might the Blessed One rob the rags upon this stone.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. And the Blessed One thought: 'What shall I take hold of when going up (from the tank)?' Then a deity that resided in a Kakudha tree, understanding, &amp;c., bent down a branch and said: 'Lord, might the Blessed One take hold of this branch when going up (from the tank).'</p>
 
 <p>   And the Blessed One thought: 'What shall I lay the rags upon (in order to dry them)?' Then Sakka the king of the devas, understanding, &amp;c., put there a great stone and sald: 'Lord, might the Blessed One lay the rags upon this stone.' </p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. And when that night had elapsed, the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him, he said to the Blessed One: 'It is time, great Sama<i>n</i>a, the meal is ready. What is this, great Sama<i>n</i>a? Formerly there was here no tank, and now here is this tank. Formerly no stone was put here; by whom has this stone been put here? Formerly this Kakudha tree did not bend down its branch, and now this branch is bent down.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. 'I had rags, Kassapa, taken from a dust heap; and I thought, Kassapa: "Where shall I wash these rags?" Then, Kassapa, Sakka the king of the devas, understanciing in his mind the thought which had arisen in my mind, dug a tank with his hand and said to me: "Lord, might the Blessed One wash the
 
 <!------------------------page 127------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_127"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 127</font></a>
 
 rags here." Thus this tank has been dug by the hand of a non-human being.</p>
 
 <p>   'And I thought, Kassapa: "What shall I rub the rags upon?" Then, Kassapa, Sakka, &amp;c. Thus this stone has been put here by a non-human being.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. 'And I thought, Kassapa: "What shall I take hold of when going up (from the tank)?" Then, Kassapa, a deity, &amp;c. Thus this Kakudha tree has served me as a hold for my hand.</p>
 
 <p>   'And I thought, Kassapa: "Where shall I lay the rags upon (in order to dry them)?" Then, Kassapa, Sakka, &amp;c. Thus this stone has been put here by a non-human being.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa thought: 'Truly the great Sama<i>n</i>a possesses high magical powers and great faculties, since Sakka the king of the devas does service to him. He is not, however, holy like me.'</p>
 
 <p>   And the Blessed One ate (&amp;c., as in chap. 16. 2 ).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. And when that night had elapsed, the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him, he announced to the Blessed One that it was time, by saying, 'It is time, great Sama<i>n</i>a, the meal is ready.'</p>
 
 <p>   (Buddha replied): 'Go you, Kassapa; I will follow you.'</p>
 
 <p>   Having thus sent away the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa, he went to pluck a fruit from the <i>g</i>ambu tree after which this continent of <i>G</i>ambudîpa (the Gambu Island, or India) is named<a name="page_127_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_127_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>; then arriving before
 
 <!------------------------page 128------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_128"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 128</font></a>
 
 Kassapa he sat down in the room where Kassapa's (sacred) fire was kept<a name="page_128_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_128_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:8"></a><font color="GREEN">8</font>. Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa saw the Blessed One sitting in the fire room; seeing him he said to the Blessed One: 'By what way have you come, great Sama<i>n</i>a? I have departed before you, and you have arrived before me and are sitting in the fire room.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:9"></a><font color="GREEN">9</font>. 'When I had sent you away, Kassapa, I went to pluck a fruit from the garnbu tree after which this continent of <i>G</i>ambudîpa is named; then I arrived before you and sat down in the fire room. Here is the <i>g</i>ambu fruit, Kassapa, it is beautiful, fragrant, and full of flavour; you may eat it, if you like.'</p>
 
 <p>   'Nay, great Sama<i>n</i>a, to you alone it is becoming to eat it; eat it yourself.'</p>
 
 <p>   And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa thought: 'Truly the great Sama<i>n</i>a possesses high magical powers and great faculties, since he is able, having sent me away before him, to go and pluck a fruit from the <i>g</i>ambu tree after which this continent of <i>G</i>ambudîpa is named, and then to arrive before me and to sit down in the fire room. He is not however, holy like me.'</p>
 
 <p>   And the Blessed One ate (&amp;c., as in chap. 16. 2).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:10"></a><font color="GREEN">10</font>. And when that night had elapsed (&amp;c., as in § 7, down to:). Having thus sent away the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa, he went to pluck a fruit from a mango tree growing near the <i>g</i>ambu tree after which this continent of <i>G</i>ambudîpa is named, &amp;c. He
 
 <!------------------------page 129------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_129"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 129</font></a>
 
 went to pluck a fruit from an emblic myrobalan tree, &amp;c., from a yellow myrobalan tree growing near the <i>g</i>ambu tree, &amp;c. He went to the Tâvatimsa heaven to pluck a pâri<i>kkh</i>attaka (or pâri<i>g</i>âtaka) flower; then arriving before Kassapa he sat down in the fire room. Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa saw (&amp;c., as in § 8).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:11"></a><font color="GREEN">11</font>. 'When I had sent you away, Kassapa, I went to the Tâvatimsa heaven to pluck a pâri<i>kkh</i>attaka flower; then I arrived before you and sat down in the fire room. Here is the pâri<i>kkh</i>attaka flower, Kassapa; it is beautiful and fragrant; you may take it, if you like.'</p>
 
 <p>   'Nay, great Sama<i>n</i>a, to you alone it is becoming to keep it; keep it yourself.'</p>
 
 <p>   And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila (&amp;c., as in § 9). 'He is not, however, holy as I am.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>   <a name="20:12"></a><font color="GREEN">12</font>. At that time one day the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas, who wished to attend on their sacred fires, could not succeed in splitting fire-wood. Now these <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas thought:</p>
 
 <p>   'Doubtless this is the magical power and the high faculty of the great Sama<i>n</i>a that we cannot succeed in splitting fire-wood.' Then the Blessed One said to the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa: 'Shall the fire-wood be split, Kassapa?'</p>
 
 <p>   'Let it be split, great Sama<i>n</i>a.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then in a moment the five hundred pieces of fire-wood<a name="page_129_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_129_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> were split. And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ
 
 <!------------------------page 130------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_130"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 130</font></a>
 
 Kassapa thought: 'Truly the great Sama<i>n</i>a possesses high magical powers and great faculties, since even the fire-wood splits itself (at his command). He is not, however, holy like me.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:13"></a><font color="GREEN">13</font>. At that time the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas who wished to attend on their sacred fires, could not succeed in lighting up the fires (&amp;c., as in the preceding story).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:14"></a><font color="GREEN">14</font>. At that time the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas, after having attended on their sacred fires, could not succeed in extinguishing the fires (&amp;c., as above).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:15"></a><font color="GREEN">15</font>. At that time in the cold winter nights, in the time between the ash<i>t</i>akâ festivals<a name="page_130_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_130_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, when snow falls, the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas plunged into the river Nera<i>ñg</i>arâ, and emerged again, and repeatedly plunged into the water and emerged. And the Blessed One created five hundred vessels with burning fire<a name="page_130_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_130_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>; at those the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas coming out of the river warmed themselves. And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas thought: 'Doubtless this is the magical power and the high faculty of the great Sama<i>n</i>a that these vessels with fire have been caused to appear here.' And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa thought: 'Truly the great Sama<i>n</i>a possesses high magical powers and great faculties, since he can create such great vessels with fire. He is not, however, holy like me.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:16"></a><font color="GREEN">16</font>. At that time a great rain fell out of season; and a great inundation arose. The place where the Blessed One livcd was covered with water. Then
 
 <!------------------------page 131------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_131"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 131</font></a>
 
 the Blessed One thought: 'What if I were to cause the water to recede round about, and if I were to walk up and down in the midst of the water on a dust-covered spot.' And the Blessed One caused the water to recede round about, and he walked up and down in the midst of the water on a dust-covered spot.</p>
 
 <p>   And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa, who was afraid that the water might have carried away the great Sama<i>n</i>a, went with a boat together with many <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas to the place where the Blessed One lived. Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa saw the Blessed One, who had caused the water to recede round about, walking up and down in the midst of the water on a dust-covered spot. Seeing him, he said to the Blessed One: 'Are you there, great Sama<i>n</i>a?'</p>
 
 <p>   'Here I am, Kassapa,' replied the Blessed One, and he rose in the air and stationed himself in the boat.</p>
 
 <p>   And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa thought: 'Truly the great Sama<i>n</i>a possesses high magical powers and great faculties, since the water does not carry him away. He is not, however, holy like me.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:17"></a><font color="GREEN">17</font>. Then the Blessed One thought: 'This foolish man will still for a long time think thus: "Truly the great Sama<i>n</i>a possesses high magical powers and great faculties; he is not, however, holy like me." What if I were to move the mind of this <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila (in order to show him my superiority).'</p>
 
 <p>   And the Blessed One said to the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa: 'You are not holy (arahâ), Kassapa, nor have you entered the path of Arahatship, nor do you walk in such a practice as will lead you to Arahatship. or to entering the path of Arahatship.'</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 132------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_132"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 132</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ. Kassapa prostrated himself, inclining his head to the feet of the Blessed One, and said to the Blessed One: 'Lord, let me receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations from the Blessed One.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:18"></a><font color="GREEN">18</font>. (Buddha replied): 'You, Kassapa, are chief, leader, foremost, first, and highest of five hundred <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas; go first and inform them of your intention, and let them do what they think fit.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Uruvelâ Kassapa went to those <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas; having gone to them, he said to those <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas: 'I wish, Sirs, to lead a religious life under the direction of the great Sama<i>n</i>a; you may do, Sirs, what you think fit.'</p>
 
 <p>   (The <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas replied): 'We have conceived, Sir, an affection for the great Sama<i>n</i>a long since; if you will lead. Sir, a religious life under the great Sama<i>n</i>a' s direction; we will all lead a religious life under the great Sama<i>n</i>a's direction.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:19"></a><font color="GREEN">19</font>. Then the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas flung their hair<a name="page_132_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_132_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, their braids, their provisions<a name="page_132_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_132_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>, and the things for the agnihotra sacrifice into the river, and went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him and prostrated themselves before him, inclining their heads to the feet of the Blessed One, they said to the Blessed One: 'Lord, let us receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations from the Blessed One.'</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 133------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_133"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 133</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   'Come, O Bhikkhus,' said the Blessed One, 'well taught is the doctrine; lead a holy life for the sake of the complete extinction of suffering.'</p>
 
 <p>   Thus these venerable persons received the upasampadâ ordination.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:20"></a><font color="GREEN">20</font>. And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Nadî Kassapa saw the hair, the braids, the provisions, the things for the agnihotra sacrifice, which were carried down by the river; when he saw that, he became afraid that some misfortune might have befallen his brother. He sent some <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas, saying, 'Go and look after my brother,' and went himself with his three hundred <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas to the venerable Uruvelâ Kassapa; having approached him, he said to the venerable Uruvelâ Kassapa: 'Now, Kassapa, is this bliss?'</p>
 
 <p>   (Uruvelâ Kassapa replied): 'Yes, friend, this is bliss.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:21"></a><font color="GREEN">21</font>. And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas (who had come with Nadî Kassapa) (&amp;c., as in § 19).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:22"></a><font color="GREEN">22</font>. And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ila Gayâ Kassapa saw (&amp;c., as in § 20); when he saw that, he became afraid that some misfortune might have befallen his brothers. He sent some <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas, saying, 'Go and look after my brothers,' and went himself with his two hundred <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas to the venerable Uruvelâ Kassapa (&amp;c., as above).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:23"></a><font color="GREEN">23</font>. And the <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas (who had come with Gayâ Kassapa) (&amp;c., as in § 19).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="20:24"></a><font color="GREEN">24</font>. <a name="page_133_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_133_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>At the command of the Blessed One the five hundred pieces of fire-wood could not be split and were split, the fires could not be lit up and
 
 <!------------------------page 134------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_134"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 134</font></a>
 
 were lit up, could not be extinguished and were extinguished; besides he created five hundred vessels with fire. Thus the number of these miracles amounts to three thousand five hundred.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 21======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="21"></a><font color="GREEN">21</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="21:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. And the Blessed One, after having dwelt at Uruvelâ as long as he thought fit, went forth to Gayâsîsa<a name="page_134_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_134_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, accompanied by a great number of Bhikkhus, by one thousand Bhikkhus who all had been <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas before. There near Gayâ, at Gayâsîsa, the Blessed One dwelt together with those thousand Bhikkhus.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="21:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. There the Blessed One thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'Everything, O Bhikkhus, is burning. And how, O Bhikkhus, is everything burning?</p>
 
 <p>   'The eye, O Bhikkhus, is burning; visible things are burning; the mental impressions based on the eye are burning; the contact of the eye (with visible things) is burning; the sensation produced by the contact of the eye (with visible things), be it pleasant, be it painful, be it neither pleasant nor painful, that also is burning. With what fire is it burning? I declare unto you that it is burning with the fire of lust, with the fire of anger, with the fire of ignorance; it is burning with (the anxieties of) birth, decay, death, grief, lamentation, suffering, dejection, and despair.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="21:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. 'The ear is burning, sounds are burning, &amp;c. . . . . The nose is burning, odours are burning, &amp;c.
 
 <!------------------------page 135------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_135"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 135</font></a>
 
  . . . . The tongue is burning, tastes are burning, &amp;c. . . . . The body is burning, objects of contact are burning, &amp;c. . . . . The mind is burning, thoughts are burning, &amp;c. . . . .<a name="page_135_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_135_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a></p>
 
 <p>   <a name="21:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. 'Considering this, O Bhikkhus, a disciple learned (in the scriptures), walking in the Noble Path, becomes weary of the eye, weary of visible things, weary of the mental impressions based on the eye, weary of the contact of the eye (with visible things), weary also of the sensation produced by the contact of the eye (with visible things), be it pleasant, be it painful, be it neither pleasant nor painful. He becomes weary of the ear (&amp;c. . . . . , down to . . . . thoughts<a name="page_135_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_135_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>). Becoming weary of all that, he divests himself of passion; by absence of passion he is made free; when he is free, he becomes aware that he is free; and he realises that re-birth is exhausted; that holiness is completed; that duty is fulfilled; and that there is no further return to this world.'</p>
 
 <p>   When this exposition was propounded, the minds of those thousand Bhikkhus became free from attachment to the world, and were released from the Âsavas.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">Here ends the sermon on 'The Burning.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the third Bhâ<i>n</i>avâra concerning the Wonders done at Uruvelâ.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 136------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_136"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 136</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 22======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="22"></a><font color="GREEN">22</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. And the Blessed One, after having dwelt at Gayâsisa as long as he thought fit, went forth to Râ<i>g</i>aha, accompanied by a great number of Bhikkhus, by one thousand Bhikkhus who all had been <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas before. And the Blessed One, wandering from place to place, came to Râ<i>g</i>agaha. There the Blessed One dwelt near Râ<i>g</i>agaha, in the La<i>tth</i>ivana pleasure garden, near the sacred shrine of Supati<i>tth</i>a<a name="page_136_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_136_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra heard: 'The Sama<i>n</i>a Gotama Sakyaputta, an ascetic of the Sakya tribe, has just arrived at Râ<i>g</i>agaha and is staying near Râ<i>g</i>agaha, in the La<i>tth</i>ivana pleasure garden, near the sacred shrine of Supati<i>tth</i>a. Of Him the blessed Gotama such a glorious fame is spread abroad: "Truly he is the blessed, holy, absolute Sambuddha, endowed with knowledge and conduct, the most happy One, who understands all worlds, the highest One, who guides men as a driver curbs a bullock, the teacher of gods and men, the blessed Buddha. He makes known the Truth, which he has understood himself and seen face to face, to this world system with its devas, its Mâras, and its Brahmâs; to all beings, Sama<i>n</i>as and Brâhma<i>n</i>as,
 
 <!------------------------page 137------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_137"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 137</font></a>
 
 gods and men; he preaches that Truth (Dhamma) which is glorious in the beginning, glorious in the middle, glorious at the end, in the spirit and in the letter; he proclaims a consummate, perfect, and pure life." It is good to obtain the sight of holy men (Arahats) like that.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. And the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra, surrounded by twelve myriads of Magadha Brâhma<i>n</i>as and householders<a name="page_137_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_137_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him and respectfully saluted the Blessed One, he sat down near him. And of those twelve myriads of Magadha Brâhma<i>n</i>as and householders some also respectfully saluted the Blessed One and sat down near him; some exchanged greeting with the Blessed One, having exchanged with him greeting and complaisant words, they sat down near him; some bent their clasped hands towards the Blessed One and sat down near him; some shouted out their name and their family name before the Blessed One and sat down near him; some silently sat down near him.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. Now those twelve myriads of Magadha Brâhma<i>n</i>as and householders thought: 'How now is this? has the great Sama<i>n</i>a placed himself under the spiritual direction of Uruvelâ Kassapa, or has Uruvelâ Kassapa placed himself under the spiritual direction of the great Sama<i>n</i>a?'</p>
 
 <p>   And the Blessed One, who understood in his mind the reflection which had arisen in the minds of those twelve myriads of Magadha Brâhma<i>n</i>as and householders, addressed the venerable Uruvelâ Kassapa
 
 <!------------------------page 138------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_138"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 138</font></a>
 
 in this stanza: 'What knowledge have you gained, O inhabitant of Uruvelâ, that has induced you, who were renowned for your penances<a name="page_138_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_138_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, to forsake your sacred fire? I ask you, Kassapa, this question: How is it that your fire sacrifice has become deserted?'</p>
 
 <p>   (Kassapa replied): 'It is visible things and sounds, and also tastes, pleasures and woman that the sacrifices speak of<a name="page_138_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_138_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>; because I understood that whatever belongs to existence<a name="page_138_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_138_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a> is filth, therefore I took no more delight in sacrifices and offerings<a name="page_138_fr_4"></a><a href="#page_138_note_4"><sup><small>4</small></sup></a>.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. 'But if your mind, Kassapa (said the Blessed One<a name="page_138_fr_5"></a><a href="#page_138_note_5"><sup><small>5</small></sup></a>), found there no more delight,--either in visible things, or sounds, or tastes,--what is it in the world of men or gods in which<a name="page_138_fr_6"></a><a href="#page_138_note_6"><sup><small>6</small></sup></a> your mind, Kassapa, now finds delight? Tell me that.'</p>
 
 <p>   (Kassapa replied): 'I have seen the state of peace (i.e. Nirvâ<i>n</i>a) in which the basis of existence (upadhi<a name="page_138_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_138_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a>) and the obstacles to perfection
 
 <!------------------------page 139------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_139"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 139</font></a>
 
 (ki<i>ñk</i>ana<a name="page_139_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_139_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>) have ceased, which is free from attachment to sensual existence, which cannot pass over into another state, which cannot be led to another state; therefore I took no more delight in sacrifices and offerings.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. Then the venerable Uruvelâ Kassapa rose from his seat, adjusted his upper robe so as to cover one shoulder, prostrated himself, inclining his head to the feet of the Blessed One, and said to the Blessed One: 'My teacher, Lord, is the Blessed One, I am his pupil; my teacher, Lord, is the Blessed One, I am his pupil.' Then those twelve myriads of Magadha Brâhma<i>n</i>as and householders understood: 'Uruvelâ Kassapa has placed himself under the spiritual direction of the great Sama<i>n</i>a.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:7"></a><a name="22:8"></a><font color="GREEN">7, 8</font>. And the Blessed One, who understood in his mind the reflection that had arisen in the minds of those twelve myriads of Magadha Brâhma<i>n</i>as and householders, preached to them in due course (&amp;c., as in chap. 7, §§ 5, 6, down to:). Just as a clean cloth free from black specks properly takes the dye, thus eleven myriads of those Magadha Brâhma<i>n</i>as and householders with Bimbisâra at their head, while sitting there, obtained the pure and spotless Eye of the Truth (that is, the knowledge): 'Whatsoever is subject to the condition of origination is subject
 
 <!------------------------page 140------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_140"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 140</font></a>
 
 also to the condition of cessation.' One myriad announced their having become lay-pupils.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:9"></a><font color="GREEN">9</font>. Then the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra, having seen the Truth (&amp;c. . . . . down to) dependent on nobody else for the knowledge of the Teacher's doctrine, said to the Blessed One: 'In former days, Lord, when I was a prince, I entertained five wishes; these are fulfilled now. In former days, Lord, when I was a prince, I wished: "O that I might be inaugurated as king." This was my first wish, Lord; this is fulfilled now. "And might then the holy, absolute Sambuddha come into my kingdom." This was my second wish, Lord; this is fulfilled now.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:10"></a><font color="GREEN">10</font>. '"And might I pay my respects to Him, the Blessed One." This was my third wish, Lord; this is fulfilled now. "And might He the Blessed One preach his doctrine (Dhamma) to me." This was my fourth wish, Lord; this is fulfilled now. "And might I understand His, the Blessed One's doctrine." This was my fifth wish, Lord; this is fulfilled now. These were the five wishes, Lord, which I entertalned in former days when I was a prince; these are fulfilled now.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:11"></a><font color="GREEN">11</font>. 'Glorious, Lord! (&amp;c., as in chap. 7. 10, down to:) who has taken his refuge in Him. And might the Blessed One, Lord, consent to take his meal with me to-morrow together with the fraternity of Bhikkhus.'</p>
 
 <p>   The Blessed One expressed his consent by remaining silent.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:12"></a><font color="GREEN">12</font>. Then the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra, when he understood that the Blessed One had accepted his invitation, rose from his seat, respectfully saluted the Blessed One, and, passing round him with his right side towards him, went away. 
 
 <!------------------------page 141------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_141"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 141</font></a>
 
 And when the night had elapsed, the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra ordered excellent food, both hard and soft, to be prepared, and had dinner-time announced to the Blessed One in the words: 'It is time, Lord, the meal is ready.' And in the forenoon the Blessed One, having put on his under-robes, took his alms-bowl, and with his <i>k</i>îvara on entered the city of Râ<i>g</i>agaha accompanied by a great number of Bhikkhus, by one thousand Bhikkhus who all had been <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas before.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:13"></a><font color="GREEN">13</font>. At that time Sakka the king of the devas, assuming the appearance of a young Brâhman, walked in front of the Bhikkhu fraternity with Buddha at its head, singing the following stanzas: 'The self-controlled One with the self-controlled, with the former <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas, the released One with the released, the Blessed One, gold-coloured like an ornament of si<u>n</u>gî gold<a name="page_141_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_141_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, has entered Râ<i>g</i>agaha.</p>
 
 <p>   'The emancipated One with the emancipated, with the former <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'He who has crossed (the ocean of passion) with them who have crossed (it), with the former <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas, the released One with the released, the Blessed One, gold-coloured like an ornament of si<u>n</u>gi go1d, has entered Râ<i>g</i>agaha.</p>
 
 <p>   'He who is possessed of the ten Noble States<a name="page_141_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_141_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>
 
 <!------------------------page 142------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_142"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 142</font></a>
 
 and of the ten Powers<a name="page_142_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_142_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, who understands the ten Paths of Kamma<a name="page_142_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_142_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a> and possesses the ten (attributes of Arahatship)<a name="page_142_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_142_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a>, the Blessed One, surrounded by ten hundred of followers, has entered Râ<i>g</i>agaha.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:14"></a><font color="GREEN">14</font>. The people when they saw Sakka the king of the devas, said: 'This youth indeed is handsome; this youth indeed has a lovely appearance; this youth indeed is pleasing. Whose attendant may this youth be?'</p>
 
 <p>   When they talked thus, Sakka the king of the devas addressed those people in this stanza: 'He who is wise, entirely self-controlled, the unrivalled Buddha, tie Arahat, the most happy upon earth: his attendant am I.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:15"></a><font color="GREEN">15</font>. And the Blessed One went to the palace of the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra. Having gone there, he sat down with the Bhikkhus who followed him, on seats laid out for them. Then the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra with his own hands served and offered excellent food, both hard and soft, to the fraternity of Bhikkhus with the Buddha at
 
 <!------------------------page 143------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_143"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 143</font></a>
 
 its head; and when the Blessed One had finished his meal and cleansed his bowl and his hands, he sat down near him.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:16"></a><font color="GREEN">16</font>. Sitting near him the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra thought: 'Where may I find a place for the Blessed One to live in, not too far from the town and not too near, suitable for going and coming, easily accessible for all people who want (to see him), by day not too crowded, at night not exposed to much noise and alarm, clean of the smell of people, hidden from men, well fitted for a retired life?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:17"></a><font color="GREEN">17</font>. And the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra thought: 'There is the Ve<i>l</i>uvana<a name="page_143_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_143_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, my pleasure garden, which is not too far from the town and not too near, suitable for going and coming, . . . . (&amp;c., down to a retired life). What if I were to make an offering of the Ve<i>l</i>uvana pleasure garden to the fraternity of Bhikkhus with the Buddha at its head?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="22:18"></a><font color="GREEN">18</font>. And the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra took a golden vessel (with water in it, to be poured over the Buddha's hand); and dedicated (the garden) to the Blessed One (by saying), 'I give up this Ve<i>l</i>uvana pleasure garden, Lord, to the fraternity of Bhikkhus with the Buddha at its head.' The Blessed One accepted the ârâma (park). Then the Blessed One, after having taught, incited, animated, and gladdened the Magadha king Seniya
 
 <!------------------------page 144------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_144"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 144</font></a>
 
 Bimbisâra by religious discourse, rose from his seat and went away.</p>
 
 <p>   And in consequence of this event the Blessed One, after having delivered a religious discourse, thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'I allow you, O Bhikkhus, to receive the donation of an ârâma (a park).'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 23======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="23"></a><font color="GREEN">23</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="23:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time Sa<i>ñg</i>aya, a paribbâ<i>g</i>aka (wandering ascetic), resided at Râ<i>g</i>agaha with a great retinue of paribbâ<i>g</i>akas, with two hundred and fifty paribbâ<i>g</i>akas. At that time Sâriputta and Moggallâna (two young Brâhma<i>n</i>as) led a religious life as followers of Sa<i>ñg</i>aya the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka; these had given their word to each other: 'He who first attains to the immortal (amata, i.e. Nirvâ<i>n</i>a) shall tell the other one.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="23:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Now one day the venerable Assa<i>g</i>i in the forenoon, having put on his under-robes, and having taken his alms-bowl, and with his <i>k</i>îvara on, entered the city of Râ<i>g</i>agaha for alms; his walking, turning back, regarding, looking, drawing (his arms) back, and stretching (them) out was decorous; he turned his eyes to the ground, and was dignified in deportment. Now the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta saw the venerable Assa<i>g</i>i, who went through Râ<i>g</i>agaha for alms, whose walking, &amp;c., was docorous, who kept his eyes on the ground, and was dignified in deportment. Seeing him he thought: 'Indeed this person is one of those Bhikkhus who are the worthy ones (Arahats) in the world, or who have entered the path of Arahatship. What if I were to approach this Bhikkhu and 
 
 <!------------------------page 145------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_145"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 145</font></a>
 
 to ask him: "In whose name, friend, have you retired from the world? Who is your teacher? Whose doctrine do you profess?"'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="23:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. Now the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta thought: 'This is not the time to ask this Bhikkhu; he has entered the interior yard of a house, walking for alms. What if I were to follow this Bhikkhu step by step, according to the course recognised by those who want something<a name="page_145_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_145_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.'</p>
 
 <p>   And the venerable Assa<i>g</i>i, having finished his alms-pilgrimage through Râ<i>g</i>agaha, went back with the food he had received. Then the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta went to the place where the venerable Assa<i>g</i>i was; having approached him, he exchanged greeting with the venerable Assa<i>g</i>i; having exchanged with him greeting and complaisant words, he stationed himself at his side; standing at his side the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta said to the venerable Assa<i>g</i>i: 'Your countenance, friend, is serene; your complexion is pure and bright. In whose name, friend, have you retired from the world? Who is your teacher? Whose doctrine do you profess<a name="page_145_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_145_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="23:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. (Assa<i>g</i>i replied): 'There is, friend, the great Sama<i>n</i>a Sakyaputta, an ascetic of the Sakya tribe; in His, the Blessed One's, name have I retired from the world; He, the Blessed One, is my teacher; and His, the Blessed One's, doctrine do I profess.'</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 146------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_146"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 146</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   'And what is the doctrine, Sir, which your teacher holds, and preaches to you?'</p>
 
 <p>   'I am only a young disciple, friend; I have but recently received the ordination; and I have newly adopted this doctrine and discipline. I cannot explain to you the doctrine in detail; but I will tell you in short what it means.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta said to the venerable Assa<i>g</i>i: 'Well, friend, tell me much or little as you like, but be sure to tell me the spirit (of the doctrine); I want but the spirit; why do you make so much of the letter?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="23:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. Then the venerable Assa<i>g</i>i pronounced to the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta the following text of the Dhamma: 'Of all objects which proceed from a cause, the Tathâgata has explained the cause, and He has explained theîr cessation also; this is the doctrine of the 'great Sama<i>n</i>a<a name="page_146_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_146_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.'</p>
 
 <p>   And the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka 'Sâriputta after having heard this text obtained the pure and spotless Eye of the Truth (that is, the following knowledge): 'Whatsoever is subject to the condition of origination is subject also to the condition of cessation.' (And he said): 'If this alone be the Doctrine (the Dhamma), now you have reached up to the state where all sorrow ceases (i.e. Nirvâ<i>n</i>a), (the state) which has remained unseen
 
 <!------------------------page 147------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_147"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 147</font></a>
 
 through many myriads of Kappas (world-ages) of the past.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="23:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. Then the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta went to the place where the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Moggallâna was. And the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Moggallâna saw the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta coming from afar; seeing him he said to the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta: 'Your countenance, friend, is serene; your complexion is pure and bright. Have you then really reached the immortal, friend?'</p>
 
 <p>   'Yes, friend, I have attained to the immortal.'</p>
 
 <p>   'And how, friend, have you done so?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="23:7"></a><a name="23:8"></a><a name="23:9"></a><font color="GREEN">7-9</font>. 'I saw, friend, the Bhikkhu Assa<i>g</i>i who went through Râ<i>g</i>agaha for alms (&amp;c.<a name="page_147_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_147_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, down to:); "But I will tell you in short what it means."</p>
 
 <p>   '"Tell me much or little as you like, but be sure to tell me the spirit (of the doctrine); I want but the spirit; why do you make so much of the letter?"</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="23:10"></a><font color="GREEN">10</font>. 'Then, friend, the Bhikkhu Assa<i>g</i>i pronounced the following Dhamma sentence: "Of all objects which proceed from a cause, the Tathâgata has explained the cause, and He has explained their cessation also; this is the doctrine of the great Sama<i>n</i>a."'</p>
 
 <p>   And the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Moggallâna, after having heard (&amp;c., as in § 5, down to the end).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 24======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="24"></a><font color="GREEN">24</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="24:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. Then the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Moggallâna said to the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sâriputta: 'Let us go, friend, and join
 
 <!------------------------page 148------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_148"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 148</font></a>
 
 the Blessed One; that He, the Blessed One, may be our teacher.'</p>
 
 <p>   (Sâriputta replied): 'It is on our account, friend; that these two hundred and fifty paribbâ<i>g</i>akas live here (as followers of Sa<i>ñg</i>aya), and it is we whom they regard; let us first inform them also of our intention; then they may do what they think fit.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then Sâriputta and Moggallâna went to the place where those paribbâ<i>g</i>akas were; having approached them, they said to the paribbâ<i>g</i>akas: 'Friends, we are going to join the Blessed One; that He, the Blessed One, may be our teacher.'</p>
 
 <p>   (The paribbâ<i>g</i>akas replied): 'It is on your account, Sirs, that we live here, and it is you whom we regard; if you, Sirs, are about to place yourselves under the spiritual direction of the great Sama<i>n</i>a, we all will place ourselves also under the spiritual direction of the great Sama<i>n</i>a.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="24:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then Sâriputta and Moggallâna went to the place where the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sa<i>ñg</i>aya was; having approached him, they said to the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sa<i>ñg</i>aya: 'Friend, we are going to join the Blessed One; that He, the Blessed One, may be our teacher.'</p>
 
 <p>   (Sa<i>ñg</i>aya replied): 'Nay, friends, do not go; let us all three share in the leadership of this body (of disciples).'</p>
 
 <p>   And a second time Sâriputta and Moggallâna said, &amp;c. And a third time Sâriputta and Moggallâna said, &amp;c. (And a third time he replied): 'Nay, friends, do not go; let us all three share in the leadership of this body (of disciples).'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="24:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. But Sâriputta and Moggallâna took with them those two hundred and fifty paribbâ<i>g</i>akas and went to the Ve<i>l</i>uvana. But the paribbâ<i>g</i>aka Sa<i>ñg</i>aya 
 
 <!------------------------page 149------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_149"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 149</font></a>
 
 began, on the spot, to vomit hot blood from his mouth<a name="page_149_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_149_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <p>   And the Blessed One saw them, Sâriputta and Moggallâna, coming from afar; on seeing them he thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'There, O Bhikkhus, two companions arrive, Kolita and U patissa<a name="page_149_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_149_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>; these will be a pair of (true) pupils, a most distinguished, auspicious pair.</p>
 
 <p>   When<a name="page_149_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_149_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a> (Sâriputta and Moggallâna), who had reached emancipation in the perfect destruction of the substrata (of existence), which is a profound subject accessible only to knowledge, came to the Ve<i>l</i>uvana, the Teacher, who saw them, foretold about
 
 <!------------------------page 150------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_150"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 150</font></a>
 
 them: 'These two companions who are now coming--Kolita and Upatissa--these will be a pair of (true) pupils, a most distinguished, auspicious pair.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="24:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. Then Sâriputta and Moggallâna went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him, they prostrated thernselves, inclining their heads to the feet of the Blessed One, and said to the Blessed One: 'Lord, let us receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations from the Blessed One.'</p>
 
 <p>   'Come, O Bhikkhus,' said the Blessed One, 'well taught is the doctrine; lead a holy life for the sake of the complete extinction of suffering.' Thus these venerable persons received the upasampadâ ordination.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="24:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. At that time many distinguished young Magadha noblemen led a religious life under the direction of the Blessed One. The people were annoyed, murmured, and became angry (saying), 'The Sama<i>n</i>a Gotama causes fathers to beget no sons; the Sama<i>n</i>a Gotama causes wives to become widows; the Sama<i>n</i>a Gotama causes families to become extinct. Now he has ordained one thousand <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas, and he has ordained these two hundred and fifty paribbâ<i>g</i>akas who were followers of Sa<i>ñg</i>aya; and these many distingtiished young Magadha noblemen are now leading a religious life under the direction of the Sama<i>n</i>a Gotama.' And moreover, when they saw the Bhikkhus, they reviled them in the following stanza: 'The great Sama<i>n</i>a has come to Giribba<i>g</i>a (i.e. Râ<i>g</i>agaha) of the Magadha people, leading with hi in all the follawers of Sa<i>ñg</i>aya; who will be the next to be led by him?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="24:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. Some Bhikkhus heard those people that were 
 
 <!------------------------page 151------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_151"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 151</font></a>
 
 annoyed, murmured, and had hecome angry; these Bhikkhus told this thing to the Blessed One. (He replied): 'This noise, O Bhikkhus, will not last long; it will last only seven days; after seven days it will he over. And if they revile you, O Bhikkhus, in this stanza: "The great Sama<i>n</i>a has come, &amp;c.," you should reply to the revilers in the following stanza: "It is by means of the true doctrine that the great heroes, the Tathâgatas, lead men. Who will murmur at the wise, who lead men by the power of the Truth?"'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="24:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. At that time the people, when seeing the Bhikkhus, reviled them in the following stanza: 'The great Sama<i>n</i>a has come, &amp;c.' Then the Bhikkhus replied to the revilers in the following stanza: 'It is by means of the true doctrine, &amp;c.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the people understood: 'It is by truth, and not by wrong, that the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as lead men;' and thus that noise lasted only seven days, and after seven days it was over.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">Here ends the narration of the ordination of Sâriputta and Moggallâna.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the fourth Bhâ<i>n</i>avâra.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 25======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="25"></a><font color="GREEN">25</font><a name="page_151_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_151_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time some Bhikkhus, as they had no upa<i>ggh</i>âyas (preceptors) and received no exhortation
 
 <!------------------------page 152------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_152"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 152</font></a>
 
 and instruction, went on their rounds for alms wearing improper under and upper garments (or, wearing their under and upper garments improperly), and in an improper attire. While people were eating, they held out their alms-bowls in which were leavings of food<a name="page_152_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_152_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, over the hard food (which the people were eating), and held them out over soft food, and held them out over savoury food, and held them out over drinks. They asked for soup and boiled rice themselves, and ate it; in the dining halls they made a great and loud noise.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. The people were annoyed, murmured, and became angry (saying), 'How can the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as go on their rounds for alms wearing improper under and upper garments, . . . . (&amp;c., as in § 1, down to drinks)? How can they make so great and loud a noise in the dining halls? They behave like Brâhma<i>n</i>as at the dinners given to them.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. Some Bhikkhus heard those people that were annoyed, murmured, and had become angry. Those Bhikkhus who were moderate, frugal, modest, conscientious,
 
 <!------------------------page 153------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_153"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 153</font></a>
 
 anxious for training, were annoyed, murmured, and became angry: 'How can the Bhikkhus go on their rounds for alms wearing improper under and upper garments, &amp;c.? How can they make so great and loud a noise in the dining halls?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. These Bhikkhus told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   In consequence of that and on this occasion the Blessed One, having ordered the fraternity of Bhikkhus to assemble, questioned the Bhikkhus: 'Is it true, O Bhikkhus, that some Bhikkhus go on their rounds, . . . . (&amp;c., down to), that they make a great and loud noise in the dining halls?'</p>
 
 <p>   'It is true, Lord.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. Then the Blessed Buddha rebuked those Bhikkhus: 'It is improper, O Bhikkhus, what these foolish persons are doing, it is unbecoming, indecent, un worthy of Sama<i>n</i>as, unallowable, and to be avoided. How can these foolish persons, O Bhikkhus, go on their rounds, &amp;c.? How can they make so great and loud a noise in the dining halls? This will not do, O Bhikkhus, for converting the unconverted, and for augmenting the number of the converted; but it will result, O Bhikkhus, in the unconverted being repulsed (from the faith), and in many of the converted being estranged.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. And the Blessed One rebuked those Bhikkhus in many ways, spoke against unfrugality, ill-nature, immoderation, insatiableness, delighting in society, and indolence; spoke in many ways in praise of frugality, good-nature, of the moderate, contented, who have eradicated (sin), who have shaken off (sin), of the gracious, of the reverent, and of the energetic. And having delivered beforethe Bhikkhus a religious 
 
 <!------------------------page 154------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_154"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 154</font></a>
 
 discourse in accordance to, and in conformity with these subjects, he thus addressed the Bhikkhus:</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, (that young Bhikkhus choose) an upa<i>ggh</i>âya (or preceptor).</p>
 
 <p>   'The upa<i>ggh</i>âya, O Bhikkhus, ought to consider the saddhivihârika (i.e. pupil) as a son; the saddhivihârika ought to consider the upa<i>ggh</i>âya as a father. Thus these two, united by mutual reverence, confidence, and communion of life, will progress, advance, and reach a high stage in this doctrine and discipline.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. 'And let them choose, O Bhikkhus, an upa<i>ggh</i>âya in this way: Let him (who is going to choose an upa<i>ggh</i>âya) adjust his upper robe so as to cover one shoulder, salute the feet (of the intended upa<i>ggh</i>âya), sit down squatting, raise his joined hands, and say: "Venerable Sir, be my upa<i>ggh</i>âya; venerable Sir, be my upa<i>ggh</i>âya; venerable Sir, be my upa<i>ggh</i>âya." (If the other answer): "Well," or, "Certainly," or, "Good," or, "All right," or, "Carry on (your work) with friendliness (towards me)," or should he express this by gesture (lit. by his body). or by word, or by gesture and word, then the upa<i>ggh</i>âya has been chosen. If he does not express this by gesture, nor by word, nor by gesture and word, the upa<i>ggh</i>âya has not been chosen.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:8"></a><font color="GREEN">8</font>. 'The saddhivihârika, O Bhikkhus, ought to observe a strict conduct towards his upa<i>ggh</i>âya. And these are the rules for his conduct: Let him arise betimes, and having taken off his shoes<a name="page_154_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_154_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> and adjusted his upper robe so as to cover one shoulder,
 
 <!------------------------page 155------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_155"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 155</font></a>
 
 let him give (to the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) the teeth-cleanser and water to rinse his mouth with. Then let him prepare a seat (for the upa<i>ggh</i>âya). If there is rice-milk, let him rinse the jug and offer the rice-milk (to the upa<i>ggh</i>âya). When he has drunk it, let him give water (to the upa<i>ggh</i>âya), take the jug, hold it down, rinse it properly without (damaging it by) rubbing, and put it away. When the upa<i>ggh</i>âya has risen, let him take away the seat. If the place is dirty, let him sweep the place.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:9"></a><font color="GREEN">9</font>. 'If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya wishes to go into the village, let (the saddhivihârika) give (to the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) his under garment, take (from him) his second under garment (i.e. his house-dress ?), give him his girdle, lay the two upper garments upon each other<a name="page_155_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_155_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> and give them (to the upa<i>ggh</i>âya), rinse the alms-bowl, and give it him with some water in it. If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya wishes (to go with) an attendant Bhikkhu, let him put on his under garment so as to conceal the three circles (viz. the navel and the two knees) and as to cover the body all around; then let him put on his girdle, lay the two upper garments upon each other and put them on, tie the knots, take his alms-bowl, after having it rinsed, and follow the upa<i>ggh</i>âya as his attendant. Let him not go too far (from the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) nor too near. Let him take (from the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) what has been put into his alms-bowl<a name="page_155_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_155_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:10"></a><font color="GREEN">10</font>. 'When the upa<i>ggh</i>âya speaks, let (the saddhivihârika)
 
 <!------------------------page 156------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_156"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 156</font></a>
 
 not interrupt him. If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya is in danger of committing an offence by the words he says, let (the saddhivihârika) keep him back. When (the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) turns back (from his alms-pilgrimage), let the saddhivihârika go back (to the Vihâra) before (the upa<i>ggh</i>âya), prepares seat, get water for the washing of his feet, a foot-stool, and a towel<a name="page_156_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_156_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>; then let him go to meet the upa<i>ggh</i>âya, take his bowl and his robe, give him his second under garment (his house-dress ?), and take his under garment. If the robe (of the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) is wet with perspiration, let him dry it a while in a hot place, but let him not leave the robe in a hot place. Let him fold up the robe. When folding up the robe, let him fold it up so as to leave (every day) four inches (more than the day before) hanging over at the corners, in order that no fold may arise in the middle of it<a name="page_156_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_156_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>. Let him the girdle<a name="page_156_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_156_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a>. If there is any food received in the alms-bowl, and the upa<i>ggh</i>âya desires to eat it, let him give water (to the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) and then offer him the food.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:11"></a><font color="GREEN">11</font>. 'Let him offer to the upa<i>ggh</i>âya (water) to drink. When the upa<i>ggh</i>âya has finished his meal, let (the saddhivihârika) give him water, take his alms-bowl, hold it down, rinse it properly without (damaging it by) rubbing, pour the water out, and dry (the bowl) a while in some hot place, but let
 
 <!------------------------page 157------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_157"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 157</font></a>
 
 him not leave the bowl in the hot place. Let him put away the alms-bowl and the robe. When he puts away the alms-bowl, let him do so holding the alms-bowl with one hand, and first feeling with the other hand under the bed or under the chair (where he is going to put the bowl), and let him not put the bowl on the bare ground. When he hangs up the robe, let him take the robe with one hand and stroke with the other hand along the bambu peg or rope on which the robe is to be hung up, and hang up the robe so that the border is turned away from him (and turned to the wall), and the fold is turned towards him. When the upa<i>ggh</i>âya has risen, let him take away the seat and put away the water for the washing of the feet, the foot-stool, and the towel<a name="page_157_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_157_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>. If the place is dirty, let him sweep the place.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:12"></a><font color="GREEN">12</font>. 'If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya wishes to bathe, let him prepare a bath. If he wants cold water, let him get cold water; if he wants hot water, let him get hot water. If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya wishes to go to the <i>g</i>antâghara<a name="page_157_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_157_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>, let (the saddhivihârika) knead the powder<a name="page_157_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_157_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a>, moisten the clay<a name="page_157_fr_4"></a><a href="#page_157_note_4"><sup><small>4</small></sup></a>, take up the chair belonging to the <i>g</i>antâghara, follow the upa<i>ggh</i>âya from behind, give him the chair, take his
 
 <!------------------------page 158------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_158"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 158</font></a>
 
 robe and put it aside, give him the powder and the clay. If he is able<a name="page_158_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_158_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, let him also enter the <i>g</i>antâghara. When he is going to enter the <i>g</i>antâghara, let him besmear his face with clay, cover himself from before and behind, and thus enter the <i>g</i>antâghara.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:13"></a><font color="GREEN">13</font>. 'Let him not sit down so as to encroach on senior Bhikkhus, nor let him dislodge junior Bhikkhus from their seats. Let him wait upon the upa<i>ggh</i>âya in the<i>g</i>antâghara. When he is going to leave the<i>g</i>antâghara, let him take up the chair belonging to the <i>g</i>antâghara, cover himself from before and behind, and thus leave the <i>g</i>antâghara. Let him wait upon the upa<i>ggh</i>âya also in the water. When he has bathed, let (the saddhivihârika) go out of the water first, let him dry his own body, put on his dress, then wipe off the water from his upa<i>ggh</i>âya's body, give him his under garment and his upper garment, take the chair belonging to the <i>g</i>antâghara, go before the upa<i>ggh</i>âya, prepare a seat for him, and get water for the washing of his feet, a foot-stool, and a towel<a name="page_158_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_158_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>. Let him offer to the upa<i>ggh</i>âya (water) to drink.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:14"></a><font color="GREEN">14</font>. 'If (the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) likes being called upon to deliver a discourse, let him call upon (the upa<i>ggh</i>âya to do so). If (the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) likes questions being put to him, let him put questions (to the upa<i>ggh</i>âya).</p>
 
 <p>   'If the Vihâra, in which the upa<i>ggh</i>âya dwells, is dirty, let him clean that Vihâra, if he is able to do so. When cleaning the Vihâra, let him first take away the alms-bowl and the robe (of the upa<i>ggh</i>âya)
 
 <!------------------------page 159------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_159"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 159</font></a>
 
 and lay them aside. Let him take away the mat and the sheet<a name="page_159_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_159_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> and lay them aside. Let him take away the mattress and the pillow and lay them aside.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:15"></a><font color="GREEN">15</font>. 'Let him turn down the bed, take it away properly without rubbing it (against the floor) and without knocking it against door or doorpost, and put it aside. Let him turn down the chair, take it away properly without rubbing it (against the floor) and without knocking it against door or doorpost, and put it aside. Let him take away the supporters of the bed<a name="page_159_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_159_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a> and put them aside. Let him take away the spitting-box and put it aside. Let him take away the board to recline on<a name="page_159_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_159_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a> and put it aside. Let him take away the carpet, after having noticed how it was spread out, and put it aside. If there are cobwebs in the Vihâra, let him remove them as soon as he sees them. Let him wipe off the casements<a name="page_159_fr_4"></a><a href="#page_159_note_4"><sup><small>4</small></sup></a> and the corners of the room. If a wall which is coated with red chalk, is dirty, let him moisten the mop, wring it out, and scour the wall. If the floor is coated black and is dirty, let him moisten the mop, wring it out, and scour the floor. If the floor is not blacked, let him sprinkle it with water and scrub it in order that the Vihâra may not become dusty. Let him heap up the sweepings and cast them aside.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:16"></a><font color="GREEN">16</font>. 'Let him bask the carpet in the sunshine, clean it, dust it by beating, take it back, and spread it out as it was spread before. Let him put the supporters of the bed in the sunshine, wipe them
 
 <!------------------------page 160------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_160"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 160</font></a>
 
 take them back, and put them in their place. Let him put the bed in the sunshine, dean it, dust it by beating, turn it down, take it back properly without rubbing it (against the floor) and without knocking it against door and doorpost, and put it in its place. Let him put the chair in the sunshine, &amp;c.<a name="page_160_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_160_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> Let him put mattress and pillow in the sunshine, clean them, dust them by beating, take them back, and lay them out as they were laid out before. Let him put the mat and sheet in the sunshine, &amp;c.<a name="page_160_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_160_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> Let him put the spittoon in the sunshine, wipe it, take it back, and put it in its place. Let him put in the sunshine the board to recline on, &amp;c.<a name="page_160_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_160_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a></p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:17"></a><font color="GREEN">17</font>. 'Let him put away the alms-bowl and the robe. When he puts them away (&amp;c., as in § 11, down to:), and hang up the robe so that the border is turned away from him and the fold is turned towards him.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:18"></a><font color="GREEN">18</font>. 'If dusty winds blow from the East, let him shut the windows on the East. If dusty winds blow from the West, let him shut the windows on the West, &amp;c.<a name="page_160_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_160_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a> If it is cold weather, let him open the windows by day and shut them at night. If it is hot weather, let him shut the windows by day and open them at night.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:19"></a><font color="GREEN">19</font>. 'If the cell is dirty, let him sweep the cell. If the store-room is dirty, let him sweep the store-room. If the refectory, &amp;c. If the fire room, &amp;c. If the privy is dirty, let him sweep the privy. If there is no drinkable water, let him provide drinkable water. If there is no food, let him provide food. If there is no water in the waterpot for rinsing the mouth with, let him pour water into the pot.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 161------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_161"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 161</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:20"></a><font color="GREEN">20</font>. 'If discontent has arisen within the upa<i>ggh</i>âya's heart, let the saddhivihârika appease him<a name="page_161_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_161_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, or cause him to be appeased (by another), by compose him by religious conversation. If indecision has arisen in the upa<i>ggh</i>âya's mind, let the saddhivihârika dispel it, or cause it to be dispelled, or compose him by religious conversation. If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya takes to a false doctrine, let the saddhivihârika discuss it, or cause another to discuss it, or compose (the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) by religious conversation.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:21"></a><font color="GREEN">21</font>. 'If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya is guilty of a grave offence, and ought to be sentenced to parivâsa discipline<a name="page_161_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_161_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>, let the saddhivihârika take care that the Sa<i>m</i>gha sentence the upa<i>ggh</i>âya to parivâsa discipline. If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya ought to be sentenced to recommence his penal discipline, let the saddhivihârika take care that the Sa<i>m</i>gha may order the upa<i>ggh</i>âya to recommence his penal discipline. If the mânatta discipline ought to be imposed on the upa<i>ggh</i>âya, let the saddhivihârika take care that the Sa<i>m</i>gha impose the mânatta discipline on the upa<i>ggh</i>âya. If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya is to be rehabilitated (when his penal discipline has been duly undergone), let the saddhivihârika take care that the Sa<i>m</i>gha rehabilitate the upa<i>ggh</i>âya.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 162------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_162"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 162</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:22"></a><font color="GREEN">22</font>. 'If the Sa<i>m</i>gha wishes to proceed against the upa<i>ggh</i>âya by the ta<i>gg</i>aniyakamma<a name="page_162_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_162_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, or the nissaya, or the pabbâganiyakamma, or the patisâraniyakamma, or the ukkhepaniyakamma, let the saddhivihârika do what he can in order that the Sa<i>m</i>gha may not proceed against the upa<i>ggh</i>âya or may mitigate the proceeding. Or if thc Sa<i>m</i>gha has instituted a proceeding against him, the ta<i>gg</i>aniyakamma, &amp;c., or the ukkhepaniyakamma, let the saddhivihârika do what he can in order that the upa<i>ggh</i>âya may behave himself properly, live modestly, and aspire to get clear of his penance, and that the Sa<i>m</i>gha may revoke its sentence.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:23"></a><font color="GREEN">23</font>. 'If the robe of the upa<i>ggh</i>âya must be washed, let the saddhivihârika wash it or take care that the upa<i>ggh</i>âya's robe is washed. If a robe must be made for the upa<i>ggh</i>âya, let the saddhivihârika make it or take care that the upa<i>ggh</i>âya's robe is made. If dye must be boiled for the upa<i>ggh</i>âya, &amp;c. If the robe of the upa<i>ggh</i>âya must be dyed, &amp;c. When he dyes the robe, let him dye it properly and turn it whenever required, and let him not go away before the dye has ceased to drop.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="25:24"></a><font color="GREEN">24</font>. 'Let him not give his alms-bowl to any one without the permission of his upa<i>ggh</i>âya. Let him not accept an alms-bowl from any one else without the permission of his upa<i>ggh</i>âya. Let him not give his robe to any one else, &amp;c. Let him not accept a robe from any one else; let him not give articles
 
 <!------------------------page 163------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_163"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 163</font></a>
