 (required for a Bhikkhu) to any one else; let him not receive (such) articles from anyone else; let him not shave the hair of any one else; let him not have his hair shaven by any one else; let him not wait upon any one else; let him not have done service by any one else; let him not execute commissions for any one else; let him not have commissions executed by anyone else; let him not go with anyone else as his attendant; let him not take any one else with him as his attendant; let him not carry any one's food received by him in alms (to the Vihâra); let him not have the food received by himself in alms carried by any one (to the Vihâra) without the permission of his upa<i>ggh</i>âya. Let him not enter the village, or go to a cemetery, or go abroad on journeys without the permission of his upa<i>ggh</i>âya. If his upa<i>ggh</i>âya is sick, let him nurse him as long as his life lasts, and wait until he has recovered.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the duties towards an upa<i>ggh</i>âya.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 26======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="26"></a><font color="GREEN">26</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="26:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. 'The upa<i>ggh</i>âya, O Bhikkhus, ought to observe a strict conduct towards his saddhivihârika. And these are the rules for his conduct: Let the upa<i>ggh</i>âya, O Bhikkhus, afford (spiritual) help and furtherance to the saddhivihârika by teaching by putting questions to him, by exhortation, by instruction. If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya has an alms-bowl and the saddhivihârika has not, let the upa<i>ggh</i>âya give the alms-bowl to the saddhivihârika or take care 
 
 <!------------------------page 164------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_164"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 164</font></a>
 
 that the saddhivihârika gets an alms-bowl. If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya has a robe and the saddhivihârika has not, let the upa<i>ggh</i>âya give the robe, &amp;c. If the upa<i>ggh</i>âya has the articles (required for a Bhikkhu) and the saddhivihârika has not, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="26:2"></a><a name="26:3"></a><a name="26:4"></a><a name="26:5"></a><a name="26:6"></a><font color="GREEN">2-6</font>. 'If the saddhivihârika is sick, let (the upa<i>ggh</i>âya) arise betimes and give him the teeth-cleanser and water to rinse his mouth with. Then let him prepare a seat (for the saddhivihârika). If there is rice-milk (&amp;c., as in chap. 25. 8, 9, down to:), and give it him with some water in it. When he expects: "Now he must be about to return," let him prepare a seat, get water for the washing of his feet (&amp;c., as in chap. 25. 10-13<a name="page_164_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_164_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, down to:). Let him offer to the saddhivihârika water to drink.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="26:7"></a><a name="26:8"></a><a name="26:9"></a><a name="26:10"></a><font color="GREEN">7-10</font>. 'If the Vihâra in which the saddhivihârika dwells, is dirty . . . . (&amp;c., as in chap. 25. 14-22).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="26:11"></a><font color="GREEN">11</font>. 'If the robe of the saddhivihârika must be washed, let the upa<i>ggh</i>âya tell the saddhivihârika: "Thus must you wash your robe," or let him take care that the saddhivihârika's robe is washed. If a robe must be made for the saddhivihârika, let the upa<i>ggh</i>âya tell the saddhivihârika: "Thus must you make the robe," or let him take care that the saddhivihârika's robe is made. If dye must be boiled for the saddhivihârika, &amp;c. If the robe of the saddhivihârika must be dyed, let the upa<i>ggh</i>âya tell, &amp;c. When he dyes the robe, let him dye it properly, and turn it whenever required, and let him not go away before the dye has ceased to drop. If the saddhivihârika
 
 <!------------------------page 165------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_165"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 165</font></a>
 
 is sick, let him nurse him as long as his life lasts and wait until he has recovered.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the duties towards a saddhivihârika.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 27======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="27"></a><font color="GREEN">27</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="27:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the saddhivihârikas did not observe a proper conduct towards their upa<i>ggh</i>âyas. The moderate Bhikkhus<a name="page_165_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_165_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> were annoyed, murmured, and became angry, saying, 'How can the saddhivihârikas not observe a proper conduct towards their upa<i>ggh</i>âyas?' These Bhikkhus told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   (Then Buddha questioned the Bhikkhus): 'Is it true, O Bhikkhus, that the saddhivihârikas do not observe a proper conduct towards their upa<i>ggh</i>âyas?' (They replied): 'It is true, Lord.' Then the blessed Buddha rebuked those Bhikkhus: 'How can the saddhivihârikas, O Bhikkhus, not observe a proper conduct towards their upa<i>ggh</i>âyas?' Having rebuked them and delivered a religious discourse, he thus addressed the Bhikkhus<a name="page_165_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_165_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>: 'Let a saddhivihârika, O Bhikkhus, not forbear to observe a proper conduct towards
 
 <!------------------------page 166------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_166"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 166</font></a>
 
 his upa<i>ggh</i>âya. He who does not observe it, is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a<a name="page_166_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_166_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> offence.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="27:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Notwithstanding this, they did not observe a proper conduct. They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I ordain, O Bhikkhus, to turn away (a saddhivihârika) who does not observe a proper conduct. And he ought, O Bhikkhus, to be turned away in this way: (The upa<i>ggh</i>âya is to say): "I turn you away," or, " Do not come back hither," or, "Take away your alms-bowl and robe," or, "I am not to be attended by you any more." Whether he express this by gesture, or by word, or by gesture and word, the saddhivihârika has then been turned away. If he does not express this by gesture, nor by word, nor by gesture and word, the saddhivihârika has not been turned away.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="27:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. At that time saddhivihârikas who had been turned away did not beg pardon (of their upa<i>ggh</i>âyas). They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that (a saddhivihârika who has been turned away) should, beg pardon (of his upa<i>ggh</i>âya).'</p>
 
 <p>   They did not beg pardon notwithstanding. They told, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that (a saddhivihârika) who has been turned away shall not forbear to beg pardon (of his upa<i>ggh</i>âya). If he does not beg pardon, it is a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 167------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_167"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 167</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   <a name="27:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. At that time upa<i>ggh</i>âyas, when the saddhivihârikas begged their pardon, would not forgive them. They told, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, forgiving.'</p>
 
 <p>   Notwithstanding this they did not forgive. The saddhivihârikas went away, or returned to the world, or went over to other schools. They told, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let him who is asked for his pardon, not withhold it. He who does not forgive, is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence:</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="27:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. At that time upa<i>ggh</i>âyas turned away (a saddhivihârika) who observed a proper conduct, and did not turn awayone who did not observe it. They told, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, who observes a proper conduct, be turned away. He who turns him away is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. And let no one, O Bhikkhus, who dues not observe a proper conduct, not be turned away. (An upa<i>ggh</i>âya) who does not turn him away is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="27:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a saddhivihârika ought to be turned away: when he does not feel great affection for his upa<i>ggh</i>âya, nor great inclination (towards him), nor much shame, nor great reverence, nor great devotion (towards the upa<i>ggh</i>âya). In these five cases, O Bhikkhus, a saddhivihârika ought to be turned away.</p>
 
 <p>   'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a saddhivihârika ought not to be turned away: when he feels great affection for his upa<i>ggh</i>âya, great inclination (towards him), &amp;c. In these five cases, O Bhikkhus, a saddhivihârika ought not to be turned away.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="27:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, it is right to turn away a saddhivihârika: when he does not feel 
 
 <!------------------------page 168------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_168"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 168</font></a>
 
 great affection, &amp;c. In these five cases, O Bhikkhus, it is right to turn away a saddhivihârika.</p>
 
 <p>   'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, it is not right, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="27:8"></a><font color="GREEN">8</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, an upa<i>ggh</i>âya who does not turn away a saddhivihârika, trespasses (against the law), and an upa<i>ggh</i>âya who turns him away, does not trespass: when he does not feel great affection, &amp;c. In these five cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, an upa<i>ggh</i>âya who turns away a saddhivihârika, trespasses (against the law), and an upa<i>ggh</i>âya who does not turn him away, does not trespass, &amp;c.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 28======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="28"></a><font color="GREEN">28</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="28:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time a certain Brâhma<i>n</i>a came to the Bhikkhus and asked them for the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. The Bhikkhus were not willing to ordain him. As he did not obtain the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination from the Bhikkhus, he became emaciated, lean, discoloured, more and more livid, and the veins became visible all over his body.</p>
 
 <p>   And the Blessed One saw this Brâhma<i>n</i>a, who had become emaciated, &amp;c. When he had seen him, he said to the Bhikkhus: 'How is it, O Bhikkhus, that this Brâhma<i>n</i>a has become emaciated, &amp;c.'</p>
 
 <p>   'This Brâhma<i>n</i>a, Lord, came to the Bhikkhus and asked them for the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (&amp;c., as above, down to:), and the veins became visible all over his body.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="28:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then the Blessed One said to the Bhikkhus: 'Now, O Bhikkhus, who remembers anything about this Brâhma<i>n</i>a?'</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 169------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_169"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 169</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   When he had spoken thus, the venerabIe Sâriputta said to the Blessed One: 'I remember something, Lord, about this Brâhma<i>n</i>a.'</p>
 
 <p>   'And what is it you remember, Sâriputta, about this Brâhma<i>n</i>a?'</p>
 
 <p>   'This Brâhma<i>n</i>a, Lord, one day, when I went through Râ<i>g</i>agaha for alms, ordered a spoonfuI of food to be given to me; this is what I remember, Lord, about this Brâhma<i>n</i>a.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="28:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. 'Good, good, Sâriputta; pious men, Sâriputta, are gratefuI and remember what has been done to them. Therefore, Sâriputta, confer you the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations on that Brâhma<i>n</i>a.'</p>
 
 <p>   'Lord, how shall I confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations on this Brâhma<i>n</i>a?'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the Blessed One on this occasion, after having delivered a religious discourse, thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'I abolish, O Bhikkhus, from this day the upasampadâ ordination by the threefoId declaration of taking refuge<a name="page_169_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_169_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, which I had prescribed. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you confer the upasampadâ ordination by a formal act of the Order in which the announcement (<i>ñ</i>atti) is followed by three questions<a name="page_169_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_169_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="28:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. 'And you ought, O Bhikkhus, to confer the
 
 <!------------------------page 170------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_170"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 170</font></a>
 
 upasampadâ ordination in this way: Let a learned, competent Bhikkhu proclaim the following <i>ñ</i>atti before the Sa<i>m</i>gha:</p>
 
 <p>   'Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, hear me. This person N. N., desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable N. N. (i.e. with the venerable N. N. as his upa<i>ggh</i>âya). If the Sa<i>m</i>gha is ready, let the Sa<i>m</i>gha confer on N. N. the upasampadâ ordination with N. N. as upa<i>ggh</i>âya. This is the <i>ñ</i>atti.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="28:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>, 6. 'Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, hear me. This person N. N. desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable N. N. The Sa<i>m</i>gha confers on N. N. the upasampadâ ordination with N. N. as upa<i>ggh</i>âya. Let any one of the venerable brethren who is in favour of the upasampadâ ordination of N. N. with N. N. as upa<i>ggh</i>âya, be silent, and any one who is not in favour of it, speak.</p>
 
 <p>   'And for the second time I thus speak to you: Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha (&amp;c., as before).</p>
 
 <p>   'And for the third time I thus speak to you: Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'N. N. has received the upasampadâ ordination from the Sa<i>m</i>gha with N. N. as upa<i>ggh</i>âya. The Sa<i>m</i>gha is in favour of it, therefore it is silent. Thus I understand<a name="page_170_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_170_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 29======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="29"></a><font color="GREEN">29</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="29:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time a certain Bhikkhu shortly after having received the upasampadâ ordination, abandoned
 
 <!------------------------page 171------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_171"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 171</font></a>
 
 himself to bad conduct. The Bhikkhus said to him: 'You ought not to do so, friend; it is not becoming.'</p>
 
 <p>   He replied: 'I never asked you, Sirs, saying, "Confer on me the upasampadâ ordination." Why have you ordained me without your being asked?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, ordain a person unless he has been asked to do so. He who does, commits a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you ordain only after having been asked.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="29:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. 'And (a Bhikkhu) ought to be asked in this way: Let him who desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination, go to the Sa<i>m</i>gha, adjust his upper robe so as to cover one shoulder, salute the feet of the Bhikkhus with his head, sit down squatting, raise his joined hands, and say: "I ask the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, for the upasampadâ ordination; might the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, draw me out (of the sinful world) out of compassion towards me." And for the second time, &amp;c.; and for the third time let him ask, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="29:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. 'Then let a learned, competent Bhikkhu proclaim the following <i>ñ</i>atti before the Sa<i>m</i>gha: "Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, hear me. This person N. N. desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable N. N.; N. N. asks the Sa<i>m</i>gha for the upasampadâ ordination with N. N. as upa<i>ggh</i>âya. If the Sa<i>m</i>gha is ready, &amp;c,<a name="page_171_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_171_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>"'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 172------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_172"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 172</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 30======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="30"></a><font color="GREEN">30</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="30:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time an arrangement had been made at Râ<i>g</i>agaha that the Bhikkhus were to receive excellent meals successively (in the houses of different rich upâsakas). Now (one day) a certain Brâhma<i>n</i>a thought: 'Indeed the precepts which these Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as keep and the life they live are commodious; they have good meals and lie down on beds protected from the wind<a name="page_172_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_172_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>. What if I were to embrace the religious life among the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as?' Then this Brâhma<i>n</i>a went to the Bhikkhus and asked them for the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination; the Bhikkhus conferred the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations on him.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="30:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. When he had been ordained, the arrangement of successive meals (with the rich upâsakas) came to an end. The Bhikkhus said to him: 'Come, friend, let us now go on our rounds for alms.'</p>
 
 <p>   He replied: 'I have not embraced the religious life for that purpose--to going about for alms; if you give me (food), I will eat; if you do not, I will return to the world.'</p>
 
 <p>   (The Bhikkhus said): 'What, friend! have you indeed embraced the religious life for your belly's sake?'</p>
 
 <p>   'Yes, friends.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="30:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. The moderate Bhikkhus were annoyed, murmured, and became angry: 'How can a Bhikkhu embrace the religious life in so well-taught a doctrine and discipline for his belly's sake?'</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 173------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_173"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 173</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   These Bhikkhus told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   (The Buddha said): 'Is it true, O Bhikkhu, that you have embraced the religious life for your belly's sake?'</p>
 
 <p>   (He replied): 'It is true, Lord.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the blessed Buddha rebuked that Bhikkhu: 'How can you, foolish person that you are, embrace the religious life in so well-taught a doctrine and discipline for your belly's sake? This will not do, O foolish one, for converting the unconverted and for augmenting the number of the converted.'</p>
 
 <p>   Having rebuked him and delivered a religious discourse, he thus addressed the Bhikkhus:</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="30:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. 'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that he who confers the upasampadâ ordination (on a Bhikkhu), tell him the four Resources.</p>
 
 <p>   'The religious life has morsels of food given in alms for its resource. Thus you must endeavour to live all your life. Meals given to the Sa<i>m</i>gha, to certain persons, invitations, food distributed by ticket, meals given each fortnight, each uposatha day (i.e. the last day of each fortnight), or the first day of each fortnight, are extra allowances.</p>
 
 <p>   'The religious life has the robe made of rags taken from a dust heap for its resource. Thus you must endeavour to live all your life. Linen, cotton, silk, woollen garments, coarse cloth, hempen cloth are extra allowances.</p>
 
 <p>   'The religious life has dwelling at the foot of a tree for its resource. Thus you must endeavour to live all your life. Vihâras, a<i>ddh</i>ayogas, storied dwellings, attics, caves<a name="page_173_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_173_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> are extra allowances.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 174------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_174"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 174</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   'The religious life has decomposing urine as medicine<a name="page_174_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_174_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> for its resource. Thus you must endeavour to live all your life. Ghee, butter, oil, honey, and molasses are extra allowances.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">Here ends the fifth Bhâ<i>n</i>avâra, which contains the duties towards upa<i>ggh</i>âyas.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 31======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="31"></a><font color="GREEN">31</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="31:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time a certain youth came to the Bhikkhus and asked them to be ordained. The Bhikkhus told him the (four) Resources before his ordination. Then he said: 'If you had told me the Resources, venerable Sirs, after my ordination, I should have persisted (in the religious life); but now, venerable Sirs, I will not be ordained; the Resources are repulsive and loathsome to me.'</p>
 
 <p>   The Bhikkhus told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'You ought not, O Bhikkhus, to tell the Resources (to the candidates) before their ordination. He who does, is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you tell the Resources (to the newly-ordained Bhikkhus) immediately after their upasampadâ.'</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 175------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_175"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 175</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   <a name="31:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. At that time some Bhikkhus performed the upasampadâ service with a chapter of two or three Bhikkhus.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, receive the upasampadâ ordination before a chapter of less than ten Bhikkhus. He who performs the upasampadâ service (with a smaller number of Bhikkhus), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. I prescribe you, O Bhikkhus, the holding of upasampadâ services with a chapter of ten Bhikkhus or more than ten.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="31:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. At that time some Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ ordination on their saddhivihârikas one or two years after their own upasampadâ. <a name="page_175_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_175_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>Thus also the venerable Upasena Va<u>n</u>gantaputta conferred the upasampadâ ordination on a saddhivihârika of his one year after his own upasampadâ. When he had concluded the vassa residence, after two years from his own upasampadâ had elapsed, he went with his saddhivihârika, who had completed the first year after his upasampadâ, to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him and respectfully saluted the Blessed One, he sat down near him.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="31:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. Now it is the custom of the blessed Buddhas to exchange greeting with incoming Bhikkhus. And the Blessed One said to the venerable Upasena Va<u>n</u>gantaputta: 'Do things go well with you, Bhikkhu? Do you get enough to support your life? Have you made your journey with not too great fatigue?'</p>
 
 <p>   'Things go pretty well with us, Lord; we get
 
 <!------------------------page 176------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_176"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 176</font></a>
 
 enough, Lord, to support our life, and we have made our journey, Lord, with not too great fatigue.' The Tathâgatas sometimes ask about what they know; sometimes they do not ask about what they know. They understand the right time when to ask, and they understand the right time when not to ask. The Tathâgatas put questions full of sense, not void of sense; to what is void of sense the bridge is pulled down for the Tathâgatas. For two purposes the blessed Buddhas put questions to the Bhikkhus, when they intend to preach the doctrine or when they intend to institute a rule of conduct to their disciples.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="31:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. And the Blessed One said to the venerable Upananda Va<u>n</u>gantaputta: 'How many years have you completed, O Bhikkhu, since your upasampadâ?'</p>
 
 <p>   'Two years, Lord.'</p>
 
 <p>   'And how many years has this Bhikkhu completed?'</p>
 
 <p>   'One year, Lord.'</p>
 
 <p>   'In what relation does this Bhikkhu stand to you?'</p>
 
 <p>   'He is my saddhivihârika, Lord.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the blessed Buddha rebuked him: 'This is improper, O foolish one, unbecoming, unsuitable, unworthy of a Sama<i>n</i>a, unallowable, and to be avoided. How can you, O foolish one, who ought to receive exhortation and instruction from others, think yourself fit for administering exhortation and instruction to another Bhikkhu? Too quickly, O foolish one, have you abandoned yourself to the ambition of collecting followers. This will not do (&amp;c.: as in chap. 30. 3). Let no one, O Bhikkhus, confer the upasampadâ ordination who has not 
 
 <!------------------------page 177------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_177"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 177</font></a>
 
 completed ten years. He who does, is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that only he who has completed ten years or more than ten years, may confer the upasampadâ ordination.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="31:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. At that time ignorant, unlearned Bhikkhus (who said), 'We have completed ten years (since our upasampadâ), we have completed ten years,' conferred the upasampadâ ordination; (thus) ignorant upa<i>ggh</i>âyas were found and clever saddhivihârikas; unlearned upa<i>ggh</i>âyas were found and learned saddhivihârikas; upa<i>ggh</i>âyas were found who had small knowledge, and saddhivihârikas who had great knowledge; foolish upa<i>ggh</i>âyas were found and wise saddhivihârikas. And a certain Bhikkhu who had formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, when his upa<i>ggh</i>âya remonstrated with him (on certain offences) according to the Dhamma, brought his upa<i>ggh</i>âya (by reasoning) to silence and went back to that same Titthiya school<a name="page_177_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_177_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="31:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. The moderate Bhikkhus were annoyed, murmured, and became angry: 'How can those ignorant, unlearned Bhikkhus confer the upasampadâ ordination (saying); "We have completed ten years, we have completed ten years?" (Thus) ignorant upa<i>ggh</i>âyas are found and clever saddhivihârikas (&amp;c., down to:), foolish upa<i>ggh</i>âyas are found and wise saddhivihârikas.'</p>
 
 <p>   These Bhikkhus told, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'Is it true, O Bhikkhus, &amp;c.?'</p>
 
 <p>   'It is true, Lord.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="31:8"></a><font color="GREEN">8</font>. Then the blessed Buddha rebuked those Bhikkhus: 'How can these foolish persons, O Bhikkhus,
 
 <!------------------------page 178------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_178"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 178</font></a>
 
 confer the upasampadâ ordination (saying), "We have, &amp;c?" (Thus) ignorant upa<i>ggh</i>âyas are found, &amp;c. This will not do, O Bhikkhus, for converting the unconverted and for augmenting the number of the converted.'</p>
 
 <p>   Having rebuked those Bhikkhus and delivered a religious discourse, he thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'Let no ignorant, unlearned Bhikkhu, O Bhikkhus, confer the upasampadâ ordination. If he does, he is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that only a learned, competent Bhikkhu who has completed ten years, or more than ten years, may confer the upasampadâ ordination.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 32======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="32"></a><font color="GREEN">32</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="32:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time some Bhikkhus whose upa<i>ggh</i>âyas were gone away, or had returned to the world, or had died, or were gone over to a (schismatic) faction<a name="page_178_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_178_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, as they had no â<i>k</i>ariyas and received no exhortation and instruction, went on their rounds for alms wearing improper under and upper garments (&amp;c., as in chap. 25. 1-6, down to:), he thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, (that young Bhikkhus choose) an â<i>k</i>ariya<a name="page_178_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_178_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 179------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_179"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 179</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   'The â<i>k</i>ariya, O Bhikkhus, ought to consider the antevâsika (i.e. disciple) as a son; the antevâsika ought to consider the â<i>k</i>ariya as a father. Thus these two, united by mutual reverence, confidence, and communion of life, will progress, advance, and reach a high stage in this doctrine and discipline.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you live (the first) ten years in dependence (on an â<i>k</i>ariya); he who has completed his tenth year may give a nissaya<a name="page_179_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_179_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> himself.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 180------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_180"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 180</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   <a name="32:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. 'And let (the antevâsika), O Bhikkhus, choose his â<i>k</i>ariya in this way: Let him adjust his upper robe so as to cover one shoulder, salute the feet (of the â<i>k</i>ariya), sit down squatting, raise his joined hands, and say: "Venerable Sir, be my â<i>k</i>ariya, I will live in dependence on you, Sir."' (This formula is repeated thrice.)</p>
 
 <p>   '(If the other answers): "Well" (&amp;c., as in chap. 25. 7).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="32:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. 'The antevâsika, O Bhikkhus, ought to observe a strict conduct towards his â<i>k</i>ariya' (&amp;c., as in chap. 25. 8-24).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the duties towards an â<i>k</i>ariya.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 33======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="33"></a><font color="GREEN">33</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   'The â<i>k</i>ariya, O Bhikkhus, ought to observe a strict conduct towards his antevâsika' (&amp;c., as in chap. 26).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the duties towards an antevâsika.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the sixth Bhâ<i>n</i>avâra.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 34======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="34"></a><font color="GREEN">34</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time the antevâsikas did not observe a proper conduct towards their â<i>k</i>ariyas (&amp;c., as in chap. 27. 1-8).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 181------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_181"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 181</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 35======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="35"></a><font color="GREEN">35</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="35:1"></a><a name="35:2"></a><font color="GREEN">1, 2</font>. At that time ignorant, unlearned Bhikkhus (who said), 'We have completed ten years (since our upasampadâ), we have completed ten years,' gave a nissaya (i.e. they received young Bhikkhus as their antevâsikas); (thus) ignorant â<i>k</i>ariyas were found and clever antevâsikas; unlearned â<i>k</i>ariyas were found and learned antevâsikas; â<i>k</i>ariyas were found who had small knowIedge, and antevâsikas who had great knowledgc; foolish â<i>k</i>ariyas were found and wise antevâsikas. The moderate Bhikkhus were annoyed (&amp;c., as in chap. 31, 7, 8).</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no ignorant, unlearned Bhikkhu, O Bhikkhus, give a nissaya. If he does, he is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that only a learned, competent Bhikkhu who has completed ten years, or more than ten years, may give a nissaya.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 36======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="36"></a><font color="GREEN">36</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus whose â<i>k</i>ariyas and upa<i>ggh</i>âyas were gone away, or had returned to the worId, or had died, or were gone over to a (schismatic) faction, were not acquainted with (the rules about) the cessation of their nissayas<a name="page_181_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_181_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>. They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'There are five cases of cessation of a nissaya, O Bhikkhus, between (saddhivihârika and) upa<i>ggh</i>âya:
 
 <!------------------------page 182------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_182"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 182</font></a>
 
 When the upa<i>ggh</i>âya is gone away, or he has returned to the world, or has died, or is gone over to a (schismatic) faction; the fifth case is that of order (given by the upa<i>ggh</i>âya to the saddhivihârika<a name="page_182_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_182_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>). These, O Bhikkhu's, are the five cases of the cessation of a nissaya between (saddhivihârika and) upa<i>ggh</i>âya.</p>
 
 <p>   'There are six cases of cessation of a nissaya, O Bhikkhus, between (antevâsika and) â<i>k</i>ariya: When the â<i>k</i>ariya is gone away, &amp;c.; the fifth case is that of order (given by the â<i>k</i>ariya to the antevâsika); or (sixthly) when the â<i>k</i>ariya and the upa<i>ggh</i>âya have come together at the same place<a name="page_182_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_182_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>. These, O Bhikkhus, are the six cases of cessation of a nissaya between (antevâsika and) â<i>k</i>ariya.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer the upasampadâ ordination, nor give a nissaya, nor ordain a novice<a name="page_182_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_182_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a>: When he does not possess full perfection in what belongs to moral practices; or does not possess full perfection in what belongs to self-concentration; or does not possess full perfection in what belongs to wisdom; or does
 
 <!------------------------page 183------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_183"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 183</font></a>
 
 not possess full perfection in what belongs to emancipation; or does not possess full perfection in what belongs to knowledge and insight into emancipation. In these five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer the upasampadâ ordination, nor give a nissaya, nor ordain a novice.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may confer the upasampadâ ordination, give a nissaya, and ordain a novice: When he possesses full perfection in what belongs to moral practices, &amp;c. In these five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. 'And also in other five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer, &amp;c.: When he does not possess for himself full perfection in what belongs to moral practices and is not able to help others to full perfection in what belongs to moral practices; or does not possess for himself full perfection in what belongs to self-concentration, and is not able to help others to full perfection in what belongs to self-concentration, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may confer, &amp;c.: When he possesses for himself full perfection in what belongs to moral practices, and is able to help others to full perfection, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. 'And also in other five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer, &amp;c.: When he is unbelieving, shameless, fearless of sinning, indolent, forgetful. In these five cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may confer, &amp;c.: When he is believing, modest, fearful of sinning, strenuous, of ready memory. In these five cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:8"></a><font color="GREEN">8</font>. 'And also in other five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer , &amp;c.: When as regards 
 
 <!------------------------page 184------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_184"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 184</font></a>
 
 moral practices he is guilty of moral transgressions; or when as regards the rules of conduct<a name="page_184_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_184_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> he is guilty of transgressions in his conduct; or when as regards belief he is guilty of heresy; or when he is unlearned; or when he is foolish. In these five cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:9"></a><font color="GREEN">9</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may confer, &amp;c.: When as regards moral practices he is not guilty of moral transgressions, &amp;c.; when he is learned; and when he is wise. In these five cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:10"></a><font color="GREEN">10</font>. 'And also in other five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer, &amp;c.: When he is not able to nurse or to get nursed an antevâsika or a saddhivihârika when he is sick, to appease him or to cause him to be appeased when discontent with religious life has sprung up within him, to dispel or to cause to be dispelled according to the Dhamma doubts of conscience which have arisen in his mind; when he does not know what is an offence; or does not know how to atone for an offence. In these five cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:11"></a><font color="GREEN">11</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may confer, &amp;c.: When he is able (&amp;c., down to:); when he knows what is an offence; and knows how to atone for an offence. In these five cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:12"></a><font color="GREEN">12</font>. 'And also in other five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer, &amp;c.: When he is not able to train an antevâsika or a saddhivihârika in the precepts of proper conduct<a name="page_184_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_184_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>, to educate him
 
 <!------------------------page 185------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_185"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 185</font></a>
 
 in the elements of morality<a name="page_185_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_185_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, to instruct him in what pertains to the Dhamma, to instruct him in what pertains to the Vinaya, to discuss or to make another discuss according to the Dhamma a false doctrine that might arise. In these:fÏve cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:13"></a><font color="GREEN">13</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may confer, &amp;c.: When he is able, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:14"></a><font color="GREEN">14</font>. 'And also in other five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer, &amp;c.: When he does not know what is an offence; or does not know what is no offence; or does not know what is a light offence; or does not know what is a grave offence; when the two Pâtimokkhas are not perfectly known to him in their entirety, with all their divisions and their whole course, and with the entire discussion according to the single rules and to the single parts of each rule. In these five cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:15"></a><font color="GREEN">15</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may confer, &amp;c.: When he knows, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:16"></a><font color="GREEN">16</font>. 'And also in other five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer, &amp;c.: When he does not know what is an offence; or does not know what is no offence; or does not know what is a light offence; or does not know what is a grave offence;
 
 <!------------------------page 186------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_186"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 186</font></a>
 
 or when he has not completed the tenth year (after his upasampadâ). In these five cases, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="36:17"></a><font color="GREEN">17</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may confer, &amp;c.: When he knows (&amp;c., down to:); when he has completed ten years or more than ten years (after his upasampadâ). In these five cases, &amp;c.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the sixteen times five cases concerning the admissibility of upasampadâ.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 37======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="37"></a><font color="GREEN">37</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   'In six cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not confer, &amp;c.<a name="page_186_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_186_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the sixteen times<a name="page_186_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_186_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a> six cases concerning the admissibility of upasampadâ.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 38======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="38"></a><font color="GREEN">38</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="38:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time that Bhikkhu who, having formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, had (by reasoning) put to silence his upa<i>ggh</i>âya, when he remonstrated with him according to the Dhamma, and had returned to that same Titthiya school<a name="page_186_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_186_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a>, came back again and asked the Bhikkhus for the upasampadâ ordination. The Bhikkhus told, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'That Bhikkhu, O Bhikkhus, who having formerly
 
 <!------------------------page 187------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_187"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 187</font></a>
 
 belonged to a Titthiya school, has put to silence his upa<i>ggh</i>âya when he remonstrated with him according to the Dhamma, and has returned to that same Titthiya school, must not receive the upasampadâ ordination, if he comes back. On other persons, O Bhikkhus, who have formerly belonged to Titthiya schools and desire to receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations in this doctrine and discipline, you ought to impose a parivâsa (a probation-time) of four months.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="38:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. 'And you ought, O Bhikkhus, to impose it in this way: Let him (who desires to receive the ordination) first cut off his hair and beard; let him put on yellow robes, adjust his upper robe so as to cover one shoulder, salute the feet of the Bhikkhus (with his head), and sit down squatting; then let him raise his joined hands, and tell him to say: "I take my refuge in the Buddha, I take my refuge in the Dhamma, I take my refuge in the Sa<i>m</i>gha. And for the second time, &amp;c. And for the third time take I my refuge in the Buddha, and for the third time take I my refuge in the Dhamma, and for the third time take I my refuge in the Sa<i>m</i>gha."</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="38:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. 'Let that person, O Bhikkhus, who has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, approach the Sa<i>m</i>gha, adjust his upper robe so as to cover one shoulder, salute the feet of the Bhikkhus (with his head), sit down squatting, raise his joined hands, and say: "I, N. N., reverend Sirs,who have formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, desire to receive the upasampadâ ordination in this doctrine and discipline, and ask the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, for a parivâsa of four months." Let him ask thus a second time. Let him ask thus a third time.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 188------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_188"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 188</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   'Then let a learned, competent Bhikkhu proclaim the following <i>ñ</i>atti before the Sa<i>m</i>gha: "Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, hear me, This person N, N ., who has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination in this doctrine and discipline, He asks the Sa<i>m</i>gha for a parivâsa of four months. If the Sa<i>m</i>gha is ready, let the Sa<i>m</i>gha impose on N. N., who has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, a parivâs-a of four months, This is the <i>ñ</i>atti,</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="38:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. '"Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, hear me, This person N. N., who has, &amp;c. He asks the Sa<i>m</i>gha for a parivâsa of four months, The Sa<i>m</i>gha imposes on N. N., who has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, a parivâsa of four months. Let any one of the venerable brethren who is in favour of imposing a parivâsa of four months on N. N., who has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, be silent, and any one who is not in favour of it, speak, A parivâsa of four months has been imposed by the Sa<i>m</i>gha on N. N., who has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, The Sa<i>m</i>gha is in favour of it, therefore it is silent. Thus I understand."</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="38:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. 'And this, O Bhikkhus, is the way in which a person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, succeeds or fails in satisfying (the Bhikkhus and obtaining upasampadâ when the probation-time is over),</p>
 
 <p>   'What is the way, a Bhikkhus, in which a person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, fails in satisfying (the Bhikkhus)?</p>
 
 <p>   'In case, O.Bhikkhus, the person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, enters the village 
 
 <!------------------------page 189------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_189"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 189</font></a>
 
 too early, and comes back (to the Vihâra) too late, thus, O Bhikkhus, a person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, fails in satisfying (the Bhikkhus).</p>
 
 <p>   'And further, O Bhikkhus, in case the person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, frequents the society of harlots, or of widows, or of adult girls, or of eunuchs, or of Bhikkhunîs, thus also, O Bhikkhus, a person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, fails in satisfying (the Bhikkhus).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="38:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. 'And further, O Bhikkhus, in case the person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, does not show himself skilled in the various things his fellow Bhikkhus have to do, not diligent, not able to consider how those things are to be done, not able to do things himself, not able to give directions to others, thus also, O Bhikkhus, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'And further, O Bhikkhus, in case the person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, does not show keen zeal, when the doctrine is preached to him or when questions are put, in what belongs to morality, to contemplation, and to wisdom, thus also, O Bhikkhus, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="38:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. 'And further, O Bhikkhus, in case the person that has formerIy belonged to a Titthiya school, becomes angry, displeased, and dissatisfied, when people speak against the teacher, the belief, the opinions, the persuasion, the creed of the school he formerly belonged to; and is pleased, glad, and satisfied, when people speak against the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Sa<i>m</i>gha; or he is pleased, glad, and satisfied, when people speak in praise of the teacher, &amp;c.; and becomes angry, displeased, dissatisfied, when people speak in praise of the Buddha, the 
 
 <!------------------------page 190------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_190"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 190</font></a>
 
 Dhamma, and the Sa<i>m</i>gha; this, O Bhikkhus, is a decisive moment for the failure of a person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school (in obtaining admission to the Sa<i>m</i>gha).</p>
 
 <p>   'Thus, O Bhikkhus, a person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, fails in satisfying (the Bhikkhus). When a person comes, O Bhikkhus, that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, and has thus failed in satisfying (the Bhikkhus), the upasampadâ ordination should not be conferred on him.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="38:8"></a><font color="GREEN">8</font>-10. 'And what is the way, O Bhikkhus, in which a person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, succeeds in satisfying (the Bhikkhus)?</p>
 
 <p>   'In case, O Bhikkhus, the person that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, does not enter the village too early (&amp;c., point by point the contrary of the preceding).</p>
 
 <p>   'When a person comes, O Bhikkhus, that has formerly belonged to a Titthiya school, and has thus succeeded in satisfying (the Bhikkhus), the upasampadâ ordination ought to be conferred on him.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="38:11"></a><font color="GREEN">11</font>. 'If a person, O Bhikkhus, that has formerly beIonged to a Titthiya school, comes (to the Bhikkhus) naked, it is incumbent on his upa<i>ggh</i>âya to get a robe for him. If he comes with unshaven hair, the Sa<i>m</i>gha's permission ought to be asked for having his hair shaved<a name="page_190_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_190_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <p>   'If fire-worshippers and <i>G</i>a<i>t</i>ilas come to you, O Bhikkhus, they are to receive the upasampadâ ordination (directly), and no parivâsa is to be imposed on them. And for what reason? These, O Bhikkhus, hold the doctrine that actions receive their
 
 <!------------------------page 191------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_191"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 191</font></a>
 
 reward, and that our deeds have their result (according to their moral merit).</p>
 
 <p>   'If a Sakya by birth, O Bhikkhus, who has belonged to a Titthiya school, comes to you, he is to receive the upasampadâ ordination (directly), and no parivâsa is to be imposed on him. This exceptional privilege, O Bhikkhus, I grant to my kinsmen.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">Here ends the exposition on the ordination of persons that have formerly belonged to Titthiya schools.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the seventh Bhâ<i>n</i>avâra.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 39======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="39"></a><font color="GREEN">39</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="39:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time these five diseases prevailed among the people of Magadha:--leprosy, boils, dry leprosy, consumption, and fits. The people who were affected with these five diseases went to <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a<a name="page_191_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_191_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> and said: 'pray, doctor, cure us.'</p>
 
 <p>   'I have too many duties', Sirs, and am too occupied. I have to treat the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra, and the royal seraglio, and the fraternity of Bhikkhus with the Buddha at their head. I cannot cure you.</p>
 
 <p>   'All that we possess shall be yours, doctor, and we will be your slaves; pray, doctor, cure us.'</p>
 
 <p>   'I have too many duties, Sirs, &amp;c.; I cannot cure you.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="39:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Now those people thought: 'Indeed the precepts which these Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as keep and
 
 <!------------------------page 192------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_192"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 192</font></a>
 
 the life they live are commodious; they have good meals and lie down on beds protected from the wind. What if we were to embrace the religious life among the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as: then the Bhikkhus will nurse us, and <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a, will cure us.'</p>
 
 <p>   Thus these persons went to the Bhikkhus and asked them for the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination; the Bhikkhus conferred on them the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations; and the Bhikkhus nursed them, and <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a cured them.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="39:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus, who had to nurse many sick Bhikkhus, began to solicit (lay people) with many demands and many requests: 'Give us food for the sick; give us food for the tenders of the sick; give us medicine for the sick.' And also <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a, who had to treat many sick Bhikkhus, neglected some of his duties to the king.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="39:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. Now one day a man who was affected with the five diseases went to <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a and said:'Pray, doctor, cure me.'</p>
 
 <p>   'I have too many duties, Sir, and am too occupied; I have to treat the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra, and the royal seraglio, and the fraternity of Bhikkhus with the Buddha at their head; I cannot cure you.'</p>
 
 <p>   'All that I possess shall be yours, doctor, and I will be your slave; pray doctor, cure me.'</p>
 
 <p>   'I have too many duties, Sir, &amp;c.; I cannot cure you.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="39:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. Now that man thought: 'Indeed the precepts which these Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as keep (&amp;c., down to:): then the Bhikkhus will nurse me, and <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a will cure me. When I have become free from sickness, then I will return to the world.'</p>
 
 <p>   Thus that man went to the Bhikkhus and asked them for the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination; the Bhikkhus 
 
 <!------------------------page 193------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_193"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 193</font></a>
 
 conferred on him the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations; and the Bhikkhus nursed him, and <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a cured him. When he had become free from sickness, he returned to the world. Now <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a saw this person that had returned to the world; and when he saw him he asked that person: 'Had you not embraced the religious life, Sir, among the Bhikkhus?'</p>
 
 <p>   'Yes, doctor.'</p>
 
 <p>   'And why have you adopted such a course, Sir?'</p>
 
 <p>   Then that man told <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a the whole matter .</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="39:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. Then <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a was annoyed, murmured, and became angry: 'How can the venerable brethren confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on a person affected with the five diseases?'</p>
 
 <p>   And <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him and having respectfully saluted the Blessed One, he sat down near him. Sitting near him, <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a said to the Blessed One: 'Pray, Lord, let their reverences not confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on persons affected with the five diseases.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="39:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. Then the Blessed One taught, incited, animated, and gladdened <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a by religious discourse; and <i>G</i>îvaka Komârabha<i>kk</i>a, having been taught . . . . and gladdened by the Blessed One by religious discourse, rose from his seat, respectfully saluted the Blessed One, and passing round him with his right side towards him, went away.</p>
 
 <p>   In consequence of that and on this occasion the Blessed One, after having delivered a religious discourse, thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'Let no one, 
 
 <!------------------------page 194------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_194"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 194</font></a>
 
 O Bhikkhus, who is affected with the five diseases, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination ( on such a person), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 40======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="40"></a><font color="GREEN">40</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="40:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the border provinces (of the kingdom) of the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra were agitated. Then the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra gave order to the officers who were at the head of the army: 'Well now, go and search through the border provinces<a name="page_194_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_194_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>: The officers who were at the head of the army accepted the order of the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra (by saying), 'Yes, Your Majesty.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="40:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Now many distinguished warriors thought: 'We who go (to war) and find our delight in fighting, do evil and produce great demerit. Now what shall we do that we may desist from evil-doing and may do good?'</p>
 
 <p>   Then these warriors thought: 'These Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as lead indeed a virtuous, tranquil, holy life; they speak the truth; they keep the precepts of morality, and are endowed with all virtues. If we could obtain pabba<i>gg</i>â with the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as, we should desist from evil-doing and do good.'</p>
 
 <p>   Thus these warriors went to the Bhikkhus and
 
 <!------------------------page 195------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_195"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 195</font></a>
 
 asked them for the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination; the Bhikkhus conferred on them: the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasanipadâ ordinations.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="40:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. The officers at the head of the army asked the royal soldiers: 'Why, how is it that the warriors N. N. and N. N. are nowhere to be seen?'</p>
 
 <p>   'The warriors N. N. and N. N., Lords, have embraced religious life among the Bhikkhus.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the officers at the head of the army were annoyed, murmured, and became angry: 'How can the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as ordain persons in the royal service?'</p>
 
 <p>   The officers who were at the head of the army told the thing to the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra. And the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra asked the officers of justice: 'Tell me, my good Sirs, what punishment does he deserve who ordains a person in the royal service?'</p>
 
 <p>   'The upa<i>ggh</i>âya, Your Majesty, should be beheaded; to him who recites (the kammavâ<i>k</i>â), the tongue should be torn out; to those who form the chapter, half of their ribs should be broken.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="40:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. Then the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him and having respectfully saluted the Blessed One, he sat down near him. Sitting near him the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra said to the Blessed One: 'Lord, there are unbelieving kings who are disinclined (to the faith); these might harass the Bhikkhus even on trifling occasions. Pray, Lord, let their reverences not confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on persons in royal service.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the Blessed One taught (&amp;c., see chap. 39. 7, 
 
 <!------------------------page 196------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_196"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 196</font></a>
 
 down to:), thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, who is in the royal service, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on such a person), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence:</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 41======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="41"></a><font color="GREEN">41</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time the robber A<u>n</u>gulimâla<a name="page_196_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_196_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> had embraced religious life among the Bhikkhus. When the people saw that, they became alarmed and terrified; they fled away, went elsewhere, turned away their heads, and shut their doors. The people were annoyed, murmured, and became angry: 'How can the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as ordain a robber who openly wears the emblems (of his deeds)?'</p>
 
 <p>   Some Bhikkhus heard those people that were annoyed, murmured, and had become angry; these Bhikkhus told the thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   The Blessed One thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'Let no robber, O Bhikkhus, who wears the emblems (of his deeds), receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on such a person), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 197------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_197"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 197</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 42======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="42"></a><font color="GREEN">42</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="42:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra had issued the following decree: 'No one is to do any harm to those who are ordained among the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as; well taught is their doctrine; let them lead a holy life for the sake of the complete extinction of suffering.'</p>
 
 <p>   Now at that time a certain person who had committed robbery was imprisoned in the jail. He broke out of the jail, ran away, and received the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination with the Bhikkhus.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="42:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. The people who saw him, said: 'Here is the robber who has broken out of jail; come, let us bring him (before the authorities).'</p>
 
 <p>   But some people replied: 'Do not say so, Sirs. A decree has been issued by the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra: 'No one is to do any harm to those who are ordained, &amp;c.'</p>
 
 <p>   People were annoyed, murmured, and became angry, thinking: 'Indeed these Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as are secure from anything; it is not allowed to do any harm to them. How can they ordain a robber who has broken out of jail?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no robber, O Bhikkhus, who has broken out of jail, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on such a person), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 198------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_198"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 198</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 43======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="43"></a><font color="GREEN">43</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a certain person who had committed robbery had run away and had become ordained with the Bhikkhus. At the royal palace a proclamation was written: 'Wherever he is seen, he is to be killed.'</p>
 
 <p>   The people who saw him, said: 'Here is the proclaimed robber; come, let us kill him' (&amp;c., as in chap. 42).</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no proclaimed robber, O Bhikkhus, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on such a robber), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 44======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="44"></a><font color="GREEN">44</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a certain person who had been punished by scourging had been ordained with the Bhikkhus. People were annoyed, &amp;c.: 'How can these Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as ordain a person that has been punished by scourging?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, who has been punished by scourging, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on such a person), is guilty of dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 45======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="45"></a><font color="GREEN">45</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a certain person who had been punished by branding (&amp;c., as in chap. 44, down to the end).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 199------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_199"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 199</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 46======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="46"></a><font color="GREEN">46</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a certain person who was in debt, ran away and was ordained with the Bhikkhus. When his creditors saw him, they said: 'There is our debtor; come, let us lead him (to prison).' But some people replied: 'Do not say so, Sirs. A decree has been issued by the Magadha king Seniya Bimbisâra: 'No one is to do any harm to those who are ordained with the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as; well taught is their doctrine; let them lead a holy life for the sake of the complete extinction of suffering.'</p>
 
 <p>   People were annoyed, murmured, and became angry: 'Indeed these Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as are secure from anything; it is not allowed to do anything to them. How can they ordain a debtor?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no debtor, O Bhikkhus, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on a debtor), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 47======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="47"></a><font color="GREEN">47</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a slave ran away and was ordained with the Bhikkhus. When his masters saw him, they said: 'There is our slave; come, let us lead him away (back to our house),' (&amp;c., as in chap. 46).</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no slave, O Bhikkhus, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on a slave), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 200------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_200"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 200</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 48======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="48"></a><font color="GREEN">48</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="48:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time a certain smith<a name="page_200_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_200_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> who was bald-headed, having had a quarrel with his father and mother, had gone to the Ârâma and received pabba<i>gg</i>â with the Bhikkhus. Now the father and mother of that bald-headed smith, searching after that bald-headed smith, came to the Ârâma and asked the Bhikkhus: 'Pray, reverend Sirs, have you seen such and such a boy?'</p>
 
 <p>   The Bhikkhus, who did not know him, said: 'We do not know him;' having not seen him, they said: 'We have not seen him.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="48:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Now the father and mother of that bald-headed smith, searching after that bald-headed smith, found him ordained with the Bhikkhus; they were annoyed, &amp;c.: 'These Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as are shameless, wicked, and liars. They knew him and said: "We do not know him;" they had seen him and said: "We have not seen him." This boy has been ordained with the Bhikkhus.'</p>
 
 <p>   Now some Bhikkhus heard the father and mother of that bald-headed smith, who were annoyed, &amp;c. Those Bhikkhus told the thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that the Sa<i>m</i>gha's permission is asked for having (the new coming Bhikkhus) shaved.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 201------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_201"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 201</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 49======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="49"></a><font color="GREEN">49</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="49:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time there was in Râ<i>g</i>agaha a company of seventeen boys, friends of each other; young Upâli<a name="page_201_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_201_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> was first among them. Now Upâli's father and mother thought: 'How will Upâli after our death live a life of ease and without pain?' Then Upâli's father and mother said to themselves: 'If Upâli could learn writing, he would after our death live a life of ease and without pain.' But then Upâli's father and mother thought again: 'If Upâli learns writing, his fingers will become sore. But if Upâli could learn arithmetic, he would after our death live a life of ease and without pain.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="49:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. But then Upâli's father and mother thought again: 'If Upâli learns arithmetic, his breast will become diseased<a name="page_201_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_201_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>. But if Upâli could learn money-changing<a name="page_201_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_201_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a>, he would after our death live a life of ease and comfort, and without pain.' But then Upâli's father and mother said to themselves: 'If Upâli learns money-changing, his eyes will suffer. Now here are the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as, who keep commodious precepts and live a commodious life; they have good meals and lie down on beds protected from the wind. If Upâli could be ordained with the
 
 <!------------------------page 202------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_202"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 202</font></a>
 
 Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as, he would after our death live a life of ease and without pain.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="49:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. Now young Upâli heard his father and mother talking thus. Then young Upâli went to the other boys; having approached them, he said to those boys: 'Come, Sirs, let us get ordained with the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as.' (They replied): 'If you will get ordained, Sir, we will be ordained also.' Then those boys went each to his father and mother and said to them: 'Give me your consent for leaving the world and going forth into the houseless state.' Then the parents of those boys, who thought, 'It is a good thing what all these boys are wishing so unanimously for, gave their consent. They went to the Bhikkhus and asked them for the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. The Bhikkhus conferred the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations on them.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="49:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. In the night, at dawn, they rose and began to cry: 'Give us rice-milk, give us soft food, give us hard food!' The Bhikkhus said: 'Wait, friends, till day-time. If there is rice-milk, you shall drink; if there is food, soft or hard, you shall eat; if there is no rice-milk and no food, soft or hard, you must go out for alms, and then you will eat.'</p>
 
 <p>   But those Bhikkhus, when they were thus spoken to by the other Bhikkhus, threw their bedding about and made it wet, calling out: 'Give us rice-milk, give us soft food, give us hard food!'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="49:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. Then the Blessed One, having arisen in the night, at dawn, heard the noise which those boys made; hearing it he said to the venerable Ânanda: 'Now, Ânanda, what noise of boys is that?'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the venerable Ânanda told the thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 203------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_203"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 203</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   'Is it true, O Bhikkhus, that the Bhikkhus knowingly confer the upasampadâ ordination on persons under twenty years of age?'</p>
 
 <p>   'It is true, Lord.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the Blessed One rebuked those Bhikkhus: 'How can those foolish persons, O Bhikkhus, knowingly confer the upasampadâ ordination on persons under twenty years of age?</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="49:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. 'A person under twenty years, O Bhikkhus, cannot endure coldness and heat, hunger and thirst, vexation by gadflies and gnats, by storms and sun-heat, and by reptiles; (he cannot endure) abusive, offensive language; he is not able to bear bodily pains which are severe, sharp, grievous, disagreeable, unpleasant, and destructive to life; whilst a person that has twenty years of age, O Bhikkhus, can endure coldness, &amp;c. This will not do, O Bhikkhus, for converting the unconverted and for augmenting the number of the converted.'</p>
 
 <p>   Having rebuked those Bhikkhus and delivered a religious discourse, he thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, knowingly confer the upasampadâ ordination on a person under twenty years of age. He who does, is to be treated according to the law<a name="page_203_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_203_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 204------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_204"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 204</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 50======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="50"></a><font color="GREEN">50</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a certain family had died of pestilence<a name="page_204_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_204_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>; only a father and his son were left; they received the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination with the Bhikkhus and went together on their rounds for alms. Now that boy, when food was given to his father, ran up to him and said: 'Give some to me too, father; give some to me too, father.'</p>
 
 <p>   People were annoyed, &amp;c.: 'These Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as live an impure life; this boy is a Bhikkhunî's son.'</p>
 
 <p>   Some Bhikkhus heard, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One, &amp;c. 'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on a boy under fifteen years of age. He who does, is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 51======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="51"></a><font color="GREEN">51</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a believing, pious family, who devoted themselves to the (especial) service of the venerable Ânanda, had died of pestilence. Only two boys were left; these, when seeing Bhikkhus, ran up to them according to their old custom, but the Bhikkhus turned them away. When they were turned away by the Bhikkhus, they cried. Now the venerable Ânanda thought: 'The Blessed One has forbidden us to confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination
 
 <!------------------------page 205------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_205"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 205</font></a>
 
 on a boy under fifteen years of age, and these boys are under fifteen years of age. What can be done in order that these boys may not perish?' And the venerable Ânanda told this thing to the. Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Are these boys able, Ânanda, to scare crows?'</p>
 
 <p>   'They are, Lord.'</p>
 
 <p>   In consequence of that and on this occasion the Blessed One, after having delivered a religious discourse, thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'I allow you, O Bhikkhus, to confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on crow-keeper boys even under fifteen years of age.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 52======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="52"></a><font color="GREEN">52</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time the venerable Upananda, of the Sakya tribe, had two novices, Ka<i>nd</i>aka and Mahaka; these committed sodomy with each other. The Bhikkhus were annoyed, &amp;c.: 'How can novices abandon themselves to such bad conduct?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, ordain two novices. He who does, is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence<a name="page_205_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_205_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 53======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="53"></a><font color="GREEN">53</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="53:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the Blessed One dwelt at Râ<i>g</i>agaha during the rainy season, and remained at the same place during winter and summer. The people were annoyed, &amp;c.: 'The (four) regions are<a name="page_205_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_205_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a> . . . . and
 
 <!------------------------page 206------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_206"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 206</font></a>
 
 covered by darkness to the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as; they cannot discern the (four) regions.' Some Bhikkhus heard, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="53:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then the Blessed One said to the venerable Ânanda: 'Go, Ânanda, take a key and tell the Bhikkhus in every cell: "Friends, the Blessed One wishes to go forth to Dakkhi<i>n</i>âgiri. Let any one of the venerable brethren who thinks fit, come to him."'</p>
 
 <p>   The venerable Ânanda accepted this order of the Blessed One (by saying), 'Yes, Lord,' took a key, and said to the Bhikkhus in every cell: 'Friends, the Blessed One,' &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="53:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. The Bhikkhus replied: 'Friend Ânanda, the Blessed One has prescribed<a name="page_206_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_206_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> that Bhikkhus are to live (the first) ten years in dependence (on their â<i>k</i>ariyas and upa<i>ggh</i>âyas), and that he who has completed his tenth year, may give a nissaya himself. Now if we go there, we shall be obliged to take a nissaya there; then we shall stay there for a short time, then we must go back again and take a new nissaya. If our â<i>k</i>ariyas and upa<i>ggh</i>âyas go, we will go also; if our â<i>k</i>ariyas and upa<i>ggh</i>âyas do not go, we will not go either. Otherwise our light-mindedness, friend Ânanda, will become manifest.'</p>
