 <p>   <a name="53:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. Thus the Blessed One went forth to Dakkhi<i>n</i>âgiri fonowed only by a few Bhikkhus. And the Blessed One, after having dwelt at Dakkhi<i>n</i>âgiri as long as he thought fit, went back to Râ<i>g</i>agaha again.</p>
 
 <p>   Then the Blessed One said to the venerable Ânanda: 'How is it, Ânanda, that the perfect
 
 <!------------------------page 207------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_207"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 207</font></a>
 
 One has gone forth to Dakkhi<i>n</i>âgiri with so few Bhikkhus?'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the venerable Ânanda told the thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   In consequence of that and on this occasion the Blessed One, after having delivered a religious discourse, thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that a learned, competent Bhikkhu lives five years in dependence (on his â<i>k</i>ariya and upa<i>ggh</i>âya), an unlearned one all his life.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="53:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. 'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not live without a nissaya (i.e. independent of â<i>k</i>ariya and upa<i>ggh</i>âya): when he does not possess full perfection in what belongs to moral practices (&amp;c., as in chap. 36. 2). In these five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu should not live without a nlssaya.</p>
 
 <p>   'In five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may live without a nissaya: when he possesses full perfection in what belongs to moral practices (&amp;c., as in chap. 36. 3). In these five cases, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu may live without a nissaya.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="53:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>-13. 'And also in other five cases, &amp;c.<a name="page_207_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_207_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>   End of the eighth Bhâ<i>n</i>avâra, which is called the Abhayûvara Bhâ<i>n</i>avâra<a name="page_207_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_207_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 54======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="54"></a><font color="GREEN">54</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="54:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. Then the Blessed One, after having resided at Râ<i>g</i>agaha as long as he thought fit, went forth to
 
 <!------------------------page 208------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_208"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 208</font></a>
 
 Kapilavatthu. Wandering from place to place he came to Kapilavatthu. There the Blessed One dwelt in the Sakka country, near Kapilavatthu, in the Nigrodhârâma (Banyan Grove).</p>
 
 <p>   And in the forenoon the Blessed One, having put on his under-robes, took his alms-bowl and with his <i>k</i>îvara on went to the residence of the Sakka Suddhodana (his father). Having gone there, he sat down on a seat laid out for him.</p>
 
 <p>   Then the princess, who was the mother of Râhula<a name="page_208_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_208_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, said to young Râhula: 'This is your father, Râhula; go and ask him for your inheritance.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="54:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then young Râhula went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him, he stationed himself before the Blessed One (and said): 'Your shadow, Sama<i>n</i>a, is a place of bliss.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the Blessed One rose from his seat and went away, and young Râhula followed the Blessed One from behind and said: 'Give me my inheritance, Sama<i>n</i>a; give me my inheritance, Sama<i>n</i>a.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the Blessed One said to the venerable Sâriputta: 'Well, Sâriputta, confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â. ordination on young Râhula.' (Sâriputta replied): 'How shall I confer, Lord, the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on young Râhula?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="54:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. In consequence of that and on this occasion the Blessed One, after having delivered a religious discourse, thus addressed the Bhikkhus: 'I prescribe,
 
 <!------------------------page 209------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_209"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 209</font></a>
 
 O Bhikkhus, the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination of novices by the threefold declaration of taking refuge.</p>
 
 <p>   'And you ought, O Bhikkhus, to confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on a novice) in this way: Let him first have his hair and beard cut off; let him put on yellow robes, adjust his upper robe so as to cover one shoulder, salute the feet of the Bhikkhus (with his head), and sit down squatting; then let him raise his joined hands and tell him to say: "I take my refuge in the Buddha, I take my refuge in the Dhamma, I take my refuge in the Sa<i>m</i>gha. And for the second time, &amp;c. And for the third time, &amp;c."</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination of novices by this threefold declaration of taking refuge.'</p>
 
 <p>   Thus the venerable Sâriputta conferred the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on young Râhula.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="54:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. Then the Sakka Suddhodana went to the place where the Blessed One was; having approached him and having respectfully saluted the Blessed One, he sat down near him. Sitting near him the Sakka Suddhodana said to the Blessed One: 'Lord, I ask one boon of the Blessed One.' (The Buddha replied): 'The perfect Ones, Gotama, are above granting boons (before they know what they are<a name="page_209_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_209_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>).' (Suddhodana said): 'Lord, it is a proper and unobjectionable demand.' 'Speak, Gotama.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="54:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. 'Lord, when the Blessed One gave up the
 
 <!------------------------page 210------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_210"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 210</font></a>
 
 world, it was a great pain to me; so it was when Nanda<a name="page_210_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_210_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> did the same; my pain was excessive when Râhula too did so. The love for a son, Lord, cuts into the skin; having cut into the skin, it cuts into the hide; having cut into the hide, it cuts into the flesh, . . . . the ligaments, . . . . the bones; having cut into the bones, it reaches the marrow and dwells in the marrow. Pray, Lord, let their reverences not confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on a son without his father's and mother's permission.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then the Blessed One taught the Sakka Suddhodana (&amp;c., see chap. 39. 7).</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no son, O Bhikkhus, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination without his father's and mother's permission. He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on a son without that permission), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 55======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="55"></a><font color="GREEN">55</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   Then the Blessed One, after having resided at Kapilavatthu as long as he thought fit, went forth to Sâvatthi. Wandering from place to place he came to Sâvatthi. There the Blessed One dwelt at Sâvatthi, in the <i>G</i>etavana, the Ârâma of Anâthapi<i>nd</i>ika.</p>
 
 <p>   At that time a family who devoted themselves to the (especial) service of the venerable Sâriputta sent a boy to the venerable Sâriputta (with this message):
 
 <!------------------------page 211------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_211"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 211</font></a>
 
 'Might the Thera confer the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on this boy.' Now the venerable Sâriputta thought: 'The Blessed One has established the rule<a name="page_211_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_211_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> that no one may ordain two novices, and I have already one novice, Râhula. Now what am I to do?' He told the thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I allow, O Bhikkhus, a learned, competent Bhikkhu to ordain two novices, or to ordain as many novices as he is able to administer exhortation and instruction to.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 56======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="56"></a><font color="GREEN">56</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   Now the novices thought: 'How many precepts<a name="page_211_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_211_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a> are there for us, and in what (precepts) are we to exercise ourselves?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, ten precepts for the novices, and the exercise of the novices in these (ten precepts), viz. abstinence from destroying life; abstinence from stealing; abstinence from impurity; abstinence from lying; abstinence from arrack and strong drink and intoxicating liquors, which cause indifference (to religion); abstinence from eating at forbidden times; abstinence from dancing, singing, music, and seeing spectacles; abstinence from garlands, scents, unguents, ornaments, and finery; abstinence from (the use of) high or broad beds; abstinence from accepting gold or silver. I prescribe,
 
 <!------------------------page 212------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_212"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 212</font></a>
 
 O Bhikkhus, these ten precepts for the novices, and the exercise of the novices in these (ten precepts).'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 57======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="57"></a><font color="GREEN">57</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="57:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time novices did not show reverence and confidence towards the Bhikkhus, and did not live in harmony with them. The Bhikkhus were annoyed, murmured, and became angry: 'How can the novices not show reverence and confidence towards the Bhikkhus, and not live in harmony with them?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you inflict punishment upon a novice in five cases: When he is intent on the Bhikkhus' receiving no alms; when he is intent on the Bhikkhus' meeting with misfortune; when he is intent on the Bhikkhus' finding no residence; when he abuses and reviles the Bhikkhus; when he causes divisions between Bhikkhus and Bhikkhus. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that in these five cases you inflict punishment upon a novice.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="57:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Now the Bhikkhus thought: 'What punishment are we to inflict?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you forbid them (certain places, for instance, their own residences).'</p>
 
 <p>   At that time Bhikkhus forbad novices the whole Sa<i>m</i>ghârâma. The novices, who were not admitted to the Sa<i>m</i>ghârâma, went away, or retumed to the world, or went over to Titthiya schools.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 213------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_213"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 213</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   'Let them not, O Bhikkhus, forbid (novices) the whole Sa<i>m</i>ghârâma. He who does so, commits a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that (the Bhikkhus) forbid (a novice) the place where he lives or which he uses to frequent.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="57:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. At that time Bhikkhus forbad the novices the use of (certain kinds of) food that is taken with the mouth. People, when they prepared rice-milk to drink or meals for the Sa<i>m</i>gha, said to the novices:</p>
 
 <p>   'Come, reverend Sirs, drink rice-milk; come, reverend Sirs, take food.' The novices replied: 'It is impossible, friends; the Bhikkhus have issued a forewarning (against us).' The people were annoyed, murmured, and became angry, thinking: 'How can their reverences forbid novices the use of all food that is taken with the mouth?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let them not, O Bhikkhus, forbid (novices) food that is taken with the mouth. He who does so, commits a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the section about punishment (of novices).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 58======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="58"></a><font color="GREEN">58</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time the <i>Kh</i>abbaggiya<a name="page_213_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_213_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> Bhikkhus laid a ban upon novices without the consent of the upa<i>ggh</i>âyas (of those novices). The upa<i>ggh</i>âyas
 
 <!------------------------page 214------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_214"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 214</font></a>
 
 searched after them, thinking: 'How is it that our novices have disappeared?' The Bhikkhus said: 'The<i>Kh</i>abbaggiya Bhikkhus, friends, have laid a ban upon them.' The upa<i>ggh</i>âyas were annoyed, &amp;c.: 'How can the <i>Kh</i>abbaggiya Bhikkhus lay a ban upon our novices without having obtained our consent?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkh us, lay a ban (upon novices) without consent of the upa<i>ggh</i>âyas. He who does, commits a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 59======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="59"></a><font color="GREEN">59</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time the <i>Kh</i>abbaggiya Bhikkhus drew the novices of senior Bhikkhus over (to themselves). The Theras, who were obliged to get themselves teeth-cleansers and water to rinse their mouths with, became tired.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, draw the followers of another Bhikkhu over to himself. He who does, commits a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 60======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="60"></a><font color="GREEN">60</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a novice, Ka<i>nd</i>aka by name, who was a follower of the venerable Upananda Sakyaputto, had sexual intercourse with a Bhikkhunî, Ka<i>nd</i>akâ by name. The Bhikkhus were annoyed, &amp;c.: 'How can a novice abandon himself to such conduct?'</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 215------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_215"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 215</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you expel a novice (from the fraternity) in the following ten cases: When he destroys life; when he commits theft; when he commits impurity; when he is a liar; when he drinks strong drinks; when he speaks against the Buddha; when he speaks against the Dhamma; when he speaks against the Sa<i>m</i>gha; when he holds false doctrines; when he has sexual intercourse with Bhikkhunîs<a name="page_215_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_215_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>. In these ten cases I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you expel the novice (from the fraternity).'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 61======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="61"></a><font color="GREEN">61</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time, &amp;c.<a name="page_215_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_215_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a></p>
 
 <p>   'Let a eunuch, O Bhikkhus, who has not received the upasampadâ ordination, not receive it; if he has received it, let him be expelled (from the fraternity).'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 216------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_216"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 216</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 62======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="62"></a><font color="GREEN">62</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="62:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time there was a certain person of an old family, whose kinsmen had died away; he was delicately nurtured. Now this person of an old family, whose kinsmen had died away, thought: 'I am delicately nurtured; I am not able to acquire new riches or to augment the riches which I possess. What shall I do in order that I may live a life of ease and without pain?'</p>
 
 <p>   Then this person of an old family, whose kinsmen had died away, gave himself the following answer: 'There are the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as, who keep commodious precepts and live a commodious life; they have good meals and lie down on beds protected from wind. What if I were to procure myself an alms-bowl and robes on my own account, and were to have my hair and beard cut off, to put on yellow robes, to go to the Ârâma, and to live there with the Bhikkhus.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="62:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then that person of an old family, whose kinsmen had died away, procured himself an alms-bowl and robes on his own account, had his hair and beard cut off, put on yellow robes, went to the Ârâma, and respectfully saluted the Bhikkhus. The 
 
 <!------------------------page 217------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_217"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 217</font></a>
 
 Bhikkhus said to him: 'How many years, friend, have elapsed since your upasampadâ?'</p>
 
 <p>   'What does that mean, friends, "years elapsed since the upasampadâ?"'</p>
 
 <p>   'And who is your upa<i>ggh</i>âya, friend?'</p>
 
 <p>   'What does that word upa<i>ggh</i>âya mean, friends?'</p>
 
 <p>   The Bhikkhus said to the venerable Upâli: 'Pray, friend Upâli, examine this ascetic.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="62:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. Then that person of an old family, whose kinsmen had died away, when being examined by the venerable Upâli, told him the whole matter. The venerable Upâli told this thing to the Bhikkhus; the Bhikkhus told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let a person, O Bhikkhus, who has furtively attached himself to the Sa<i>m</i>gha, if he has not received the upasampadâ ordination, not receive it; if he has received it, let him be expelled (from the fraternity).</p>
 
 <p>   'Let a person, O Bhikkhus, who has gone over to the Titthiyas' ( &amp;c., as in chap. 61).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 63======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="63"></a><font color="GREEN">63</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="63:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time there was a serpent who was aggrieved at, ashamed of, and conceived aversion for his having been born as a serpent. Now this serpent thought: 'What am I to do in order to become released from being a serpent, and quickly to obtain human nature?' Then this serpent gave himself the following answer: 'These Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as lead indeed a virtuous, tranquil, holy life; they speak the truth; they keep the precepts of morality, and are endowed with all virtues. If 
 
 <!------------------------page 218------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_218"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 218</font></a>
 
 I could obtain pabba<i>gg</i>â with the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as, I should be released from bcing a serpent and quickly obtain human nature,'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="63:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then that serpent, in the shape of a youth, went to the Bhikkhus, and asked them for the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination; the Bhikkhus conferred on him the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations.</p>
 
 <p>   At that time that serpent dwelt together with a certain Bhikkhu in the last Vihâra (near the boundary wall of the <i>G</i>etavana). Now that Bhikkhu, having arisen in the night, at dawn, was walking up and down in the open air. When that Bhikkhu had left (the Vihâra), that serpent, who thought himself safe (from discovery), fell asleep (in his natural shape). The whole Vihâra was filled with the snake's body; his windings jutted out of the window.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="63:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. Then that Bhikkhu thought: 'I will go back to the Vihâra,' opened the door, and saw the whole Vihâra filled with the snake's body, the windings jutting out of the window. Seeing that he was terrified and cried out. The Bhikkhus ran up, and said to that Bhikkhu: 'Why did you cry out, friend?' 'This whole Vihâra, friends, is filled with a snake's body; the windings jut out of the window.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then that serpent awoke from that noise and sat down on his seat. The Bhikkhus said to him: 'Who are you, friend?' 'I am a serpent, reverend Sirs.' 'And why have you done such a thing, friend?' Then that Nâga told the whole matter to the Bhikkhus; the Bhikkhus told it to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="63:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. In consequence of that and on this occasion the Blessed One, having ordered the fraternity of 
 
 <!------------------------page 219------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_219"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 219</font></a>
 
 Bhikkhus to assemble, said to that serpent: 'You serpents are not capable of (spiritual) growth in this doctrine and discipline. However, serpent, go and observe fast on the fourteenth, fifteenth, and eighth day of each half month; thus will you be released from being a serpent and quickly obtain human nature.'</p>
 
 <p>   Then that serpent, who thought, 'I am not capable of (spiritual) growth in this doctrine and discipline,' became sad and sorrowful, shed tears, made an outcry, and went away.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="63:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. Then the Blessed One said to the Bhikkhus:</p>
 
 <p>   'There are two occasions, O Bhikkhus, on which a serpent (who has assumed human shape) manifests his true nature: when he has sexual intercourse with a female of his species, and if he thinks himself safe (from discovery) and falls asleep. These, O Bhikkhus, are the two occasions on which a serpent manifests his true nature.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let an animal, O Bhikkhus, that has not received the upasampadâ ordination, not receive it; if it has received it, let it be expelled (from the fraternity).'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 64======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="64"></a><font color="GREEN">64</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="64:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time a certain young man deprived his mother of life. He was grieved, ashamed, and loathed this sinful deed. Now this young man thought: 'What am I to do to get rid of my sinful deed?' Then this young man gave himself this answer: 'These Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as  lead indeed a virtuous, tranquil, holy life, &amp;c. If I could obtain 
 
 <!------------------------page 220------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_220"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 220</font></a>
 
 pabba<i>gg</i>â with the Sakyaputtiya Sama<i>n</i>as, I might get rid of my sinful deed.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="64:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then that young man went to the Bhikkhus and asked them for the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. The Bhikkhus said to the venerable Upâli: 'Formerly , friend Upâli, a serpent in the shape of a youth received the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination with the Bhikkhus; pray, friend Upâli, examine this young man.' Then that young man, when examined by the venerable Upâli, told him the whole matter. The venerable Upâli told it to the Bhikkhus; the Bhikkhus told it to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let a person, O Bhikkhus, that is guilty of matricide, if he has not received the upasampadâ ordination, not receive it; if he has received it, let him be expelled (from the fraternity).'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 65======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="65"></a><font color="GREEN">65</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a certain young man deprived his father of life (&amp;c., as in chap.64).</p>
 
 <p>   'Let a person, O Bhikkhus, that is guilty of parricide, &amp;c.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 66======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="66"></a><font color="GREEN">66</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="66:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time a number of Bhikkhus were travelling on the road from Sâketa to Sâvatthi. On the road robbers broke forth, robbed some of the Bhikkhus, and killed some of them. Then royal soldiers came from Sâvatthi and caught some of the robbers; others of them escaped. Those who had escaped, received pabba<i>gg</i>â with the Bhikkhus; those who had been caught, were led to death.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 221------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_221"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 221</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   <a name="66:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then those who had been ordained, saw those robbers who were being led to death; seeing them they said: 'It is well that we have escaped; had we been caught, we should also be killed thus.' The Bhikkhus said to them: 'Why, what have you done, friends?' Then those (robbers) who had been ordained, told the whole matter to the Bhikkhus. The Bhikkhus told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Those Bhikkhus, O Bhikkhus, were Arahats. Let a person, O Bhikkhus, that has murdered an Arahat, if this person has not received the upasampadâ ordination, not receive it; if he has received it, let him be expelled (from the fraternity).'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 67======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="67"></a><font color="GREEN">67</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a number of Bhikkhunîs were travelling on the road from Sâketa to Sâvatthi. On the road robbers broke forth, robbed some of the Bhikkhunîs, and violated some of them. Then royal soldiers (&amp;c., as in chap. 66).</p>
 
 <p>   The Bhikkhus told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let a person, O Bhikkhus, that has violated a Bhikkhunî (or, that has had sexual intercourse with a Bhikkhunî), (&amp;c., as in chap. 66).</p>
 
 <p>   'Let a person, O Bhikkhus, that has caused a schism among the Sa<i>m</i>gha, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let a person, O Bhikkhus, that has shed (a Buddha's) blood,' &amp;c.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 222------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_222"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 222</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 68======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="68"></a><font color="GREEN">68</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time a certain hermaphrodite had received pabba<i>gg</i>â with the Bhikkhus; so karoti pi kârâpeti pi.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let a hermaphrodite, O Bhikkhus,' &amp;c.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 69======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="69"></a><font color="GREEN">69</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="69:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred, the upasampadâ ordination on a person that had no upa<i>ggh</i>âya.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, who has no upa<i>ggh</i>âya, receive the upasampadâ ordination. He who confers the upasampadâ ordination (on such a person), commits a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="69:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ ordination with the Sa<i>m</i>gha as upa<i>ggh</i>âya.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one receive the upasampadâ ordination with the Sa<i>m</i>gha as upa<i>ggh</i>âya. He who confers the upasampadâ ordination (in such a way), commits a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="69:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ ordination with a number of Bhikkhus<a name="page_222_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_222_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> as upa<i>ggh</i>âya (&amp;c., as before).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="69:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ
 
 <!------------------------page 223------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_223"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 223</font></a>
 
 ordination with a eunuch as upa<i>ggh</i>âya, &amp;c.; with a person that had furtively attached himself (to the Sa<i>m</i>gha) as upa<i>ggh</i>âya; with a person that was gone over to the Titthiyas as upa<i>ggh</i>âya; with an animal as upa<i>ggh</i>âya; with a person that was guilty of matricide as upa<i>ggh</i>âya; with a person that was guilty of parricide as upa<i>ggh</i>âya; with a person that had murdered an Arahat as upa<i>ggh</i>âya; with a person that had violated a Bhikkhunî as upa<i>ggh</i>âya; with a person that had caused a schism among the Sa<i>m</i>gha as upa<i>ggh</i>âya; with a person that had shed (a Buddha's) blood as upa<i>ggh</i>âya; with a hermaphrodite as upa<i>ggh</i>âya.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one,' &amp;c. (as in the first clause).</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 70======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="70"></a><font color="GREEN">70</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="70:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ ordination on persons that had no alms-bowl. They received alms with their hands. People were annoyed, murmured, and became angry, saying, 'Like the Titthiyas.'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, receive the upasampadâ ordination without having an alms-bowl. He who confers the upasampadâ ordination (on a person that has not), commits a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="70:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ ordination on persons that had no robes. They went out for alms naked. People were annoyed (&amp;c., as in § 1).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="70:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ 
 
 <!------------------------page 224------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_224"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 224</font></a>
 
 ordination on persons that had neither alms-bowl nor robes. They went out for alms naked and (received alms) with their hands. People were annoyed (&amp;c., as in § 1).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="70:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ ordination on persons that had borrowed alms-bowls. After the ordination (the owners) took their alms-bowls back; (the Bhikkhus) received alms with their hands. People were annoyed (&amp;c. . . . . down to): 'Like the Titthiyas.'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, receive the upasampadâ ordination who has borrowed the alms-bowl. He who confers,' &amp;c. (as in the first clause).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="70:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ ordination on persons that had borrowed robes. After the ordination (the owners) took their robes back; (the Bhikkhus) went out for alms naked. People were annoyed (&amp;c., as in § 1 to the end).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="70:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the upasampadâ ordination on persons that had borrowed alms-bowls and robes, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>   Here end the twenty cases in which upasampadâ is forbidden.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 71======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="71"></a><font color="GREEN">71</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="71:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus conferred the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination on a person whose hands were cut off, on a person whose feet were cut off, whose hands and feet were cut off, whose ears were cut off, whose nose was cut off, whose ears and nose were cut off, whose fingers were cut off, whose 
 
 <!------------------------page 225------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_225"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 225</font></a>
 
 thumbs were cut off, whose tendons (of the feet) were cut, who had hands like a snake's hood<a name="page_225_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_225_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, who was a hump-back, or a dwarf, or a person that had a goitre, that had been branded, that had been scourged, on a proclaimed robber, on a person that had elephantiasis, that was afflicted with bad illness, that gave offence (by any deformity) to those who saw him, on a one-eyed person, on a person with a crooked limb, on a lame person, on a person that was paralysed on one side, on a cripple<a name="page_225_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_225_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>, on a person weak from age, on a blind man, on a dumb man, on a deaf man, on a blind and dumb man, on a blind and deaf man, on a deaf and dumb man, on a blind, deaf and dumb man.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no person, O Bhikkhus, whose hands are cut off, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination. Let no person whose feet are cut off, receive the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination, &amp;c. (each of the above cases being here repeated). He who confers the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination (on such persons), is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>   Here end the thirty-two cases in which pabba<i>gg</i>â. is forbidden.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the ninth Bhâ<i>n</i>avâra.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 226------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_226"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 226</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 72======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="72"></a><font color="GREEN">72</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="72:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the <i>Kh</i>abbaggiya Bhikkhus gave a nissaya to shameless Bhikkhus.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, give a nissaya to shameless Bhikkhus. He who does, is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <p>   At that time some Bhikkhus lived in dependence on shameless Bhikkhus (i.e. they received a nissaya from them, they chose them for their upa<i>ggh</i>âyas or â<i>k</i>ariyas); ere long they became also shameless, bad Bhikkhus.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, live in dependence on shameless Bhikkhus. He who does, is guilty of a dukka<i>t</i>a offence.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="72:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Now the Bhikkhus thought: 'The Blessed One has prescribed that we shall not give a nissaya to shameless Bhikkhus, nor live in dependence on shameless Bhikkhus. Now how are we to discern modest and shameless persons?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you wait first four or five days until you have seen how a Bhikkhu behaves to the other Bhikkhus.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 73======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="73"></a><font color="GREEN">73</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="73:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time a certain Bhikkhu was travelling on the road in the Kosala country. Now this Bhikkhu thought: 'The Blessed One has prescribed that we shall not live without a nissaya (of an â<i>k</i>ariya and 
 
 <!------------------------page 227------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_227"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 227</font></a>
 
 an upa<i>ggh</i>âya); now I want a nissaya, but I am travelling. What am I to do?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I allow, O Bhikkhus, a travelling Bhikkhu who can get no nissaya, to live without a nissaya.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="73:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. At that time two Bhikkhus were travelling on the road in the Kosala country. They came to a certain residence; there one of the two Bhikkhus was taken ill. Now that sick Bhikkhu thought: 'The Blessed One has prescribed that we shall not live without a nissaya; now I want a nissaya, but I am sick. What am I to do?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I allow, O Bhikkhus, a sick Bhikkhu who can get no nissaya, to live without a nissaya.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="73:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. Now the other Bhikkhu, who nursed that sick Bhikkhu, thought: 'The Blessed One has prescribed, &amp;c.; now I want a nissaya, but this Bhikkhu is sick. What am I to do?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I allow, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu who is nursing a sick Bhikkhu, if he can get no nissaya and the sick asks him (to remain with him), to live without a nissaya.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="73:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. At that time a certain Bhikkhu lived in the forest; he had a dwelling-place where he lived pleasantly. Now this Bhikkhu thought: 'The Blessed One has prescribed, &amp;c.; now I want a nissaya, but I live in the forest and have a dwelling-place where I live pleasantly. What am I to do?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I allow, O Bhikkhus, a Bhikkhu living in the forest who finds a place where he may live pleasantly, 
 
 <!------------------------page 228------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_228"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 228</font></a>
 
  and who can get (there) no nissaya, to live without a nissaya (saying to himself): "If a proper person to give me nissaya comes hither, I will take nissaya of that person."</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 74======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="74"></a><font color="GREEN">74</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="74:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time there was a person that desired to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable Mahâkassapa. Then the venerable Mahâkassapa sent a messenger to the venerable Ânanda: 'Come, Ânanda, and recite the upasampadâ proclamation for this person.' The venerable Ânanda said: 'I cannot pronounce the Thera's (i.e. Mahâkassapa's) name; the Thera is too venerable compared with me.'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I allow you, O Bhikkhus, to use also the family name (of the upa<i>ggh</i>âya, instead of his proper name) in the proclamation.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="74:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. At that time there were two persons that desired to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable Mahâkassapa. They quarrelled with each other. (One said): 'I will receive the upasampadâ ordination first. ' (The other said): 'Nay, I will receive it first.' . They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I allow you, O Bhikkhus, to ordain two persons by one proclamation.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="74:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. At that time there were persons who desired to receive the upasampadâ ordination from different Theras. They quarrelled with each other. (One said); , 1 will receive the upasampadâ ordination 
 
 <!------------------------page 229------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_229"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 229</font></a>
 
 first.' (The other said): 'Nay, I will receive it first.' The Theras said: 'Well, friends, let us ordain them altogether by one proclamation.'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I allow you, O Bhikkhus, to ordain two or three persons by one proclamation, provided they have the same upa<i>ggh</i>âya, but not if they have different upa<i>ggh</i>âyas.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 75======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="75"></a><font color="GREEN">75</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   At that time the venerable Kumârakassapa had received the upasampadâ ordination when he had completed the twentieth year from his conception (but not from his birth). Now the venerable Kumârakassapa thought: 'The Blessed One has forbidden us to confer the upasampadâ ordination on persons under twenty years of age<a name="page_229_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_229_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, and I have completed my twentieth year (only) from my conception. Have I, therefore, received the upasampadâ ordination, or have I not received it?'</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'When, O Bhikkhus, in the womb the first thought rises up (in the nascent being), the first consciousness manifests itself, according to this the (true) birth should be reckoned. I allow you, O Bhikkhus, to confer the upasampadâ ordination on persons that have completed the twentieth year from their conception (only).'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 230------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_230"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 230</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 76======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="76"></a><font color="GREEN">76</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time ordained Bhikkhus were seen who were afflicted with leprosy, boils, dry leprosy, consumption, and fits.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that he who confers the upasampadâ ordination, ask (the person to be ordained) about the Disqualifications (for receiving the ordination). And let him ask, O Bhikkhus, in this way:</p>
 
 <p>   'Are you afflicted with the following diseases, leprosy, boils, dry leprosy, consumption, and fits?</p>
 
 <p>   'Are you a man?</p>
 
 <p>   'Are you a male?</p>
 
 <p>   'Are you a freeman?</p>
 
 <p>   'Have you no debts?</p>
 
 <p>   'Are you not in the royal service?</p>
 
 <p>   'Have your father and mother given their consent?</p>
 
 <p>   'Are you full twenty years old?</p>
 
 <p>   'Are your alms-bowl and your robes in due state?</p>
 
 <p>   'What is your name?</p>
 
 <p>   'What is your upa<i>ggh</i>âya's name?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus asked the persons who desired to receive the upasampadâ ordination about the Disqualifications, without having them instructed beforehand (how to answer). The persons that desired to be ordained, became disconcerted, perplexed, and could not answer.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you first instruct (the persons desirous of being ordained), and then ask them about the Disqualifications.'</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 231------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_231"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 231</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. Then they instructed (the candidates) in the midst of the assembly; the persons desirous of being ordained became disconcerted, perplexed, and could not answer nevertheless.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you instruct them aside, and ask them about the Disqualifications before the assembly. And you ought, O Bhikkhus, to instruct them in this way: You ought first to cause them to choose an upa<i>ggh</i>âya; when they have chosen an upa<i>ggh</i>âya, their alms-bowl and robes must be shown to them, "This is your alms-bowl, this is your sa<i>m</i>ghâ<i>t</i>i, this is your upper robe, this is your under garment; come and place yourself here."'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. Ignorant, unlearned Bhikkhus instructed them; the persons desirous of being ordained, though they had been instructed, became disconcerted, perplexed, and could not answer.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no ignorant, unlearned Bhikkhus, O Bhikkhus, instruct them. If they do, they commit a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that a learned, competent Bhikkhu instruct them.'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. At. that time persons instructed them who were not appointed thereto.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let no one, O Bhikkhus, instruct them without being appointed thereto. He who so instructs, commits a dukka<i>t</i>a offence. I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that an appointed Bhikkhu is to instruct them. And (this Bhikkhu), O Bhikkhus, is to be appointed in this way: One may either appoint himself, or one may appoint another person. And how is (a Bhikkhu) to 
 
 <!------------------------page 232------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_232"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 232</font></a>
 
 appoint himself? Let a learned, competent Bhikkhu proclaim the following <i>ñ</i>atti before the Sa<i>m</i>gha: "Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, hear me. N. N. desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable N. N. If the Sa<i>m</i>gha is ready, I will instruct N. N." Thus one may appoint himself.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:6"></a><font color="GREEN">6</font>. 'And how is (a Bhikkhu) to appoint another person? Let a learned, competent Bhikkhu proclaim the following <i>ñ</i>atti before the Sa<i>m</i>gha: "Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, &amp;c. N. N. desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable N. N. If the Sa<i>m</i>gha is ready let N. N. instruct N. N." Thus one may appoint another person.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:7"></a><font color="GREEN">7</font>. 'Then let that appointed Bhikkhu go to the person who desires to be ordained, and thus address him: "Do you hear, N. N.? This is the time for you to speak the truth, and to say that which is. When I ask you before the assembly about that which is, you ought, if it is so, to answer: 'It is;' if it is not so, you ought to answer: 'It is not.' Be not disconcerted, be not perplexed. I shall ask you thus: 'Are you afflicted with the following diseases, &amp;c?'"'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:8"></a><font color="GREEN">8</font>. (After the instruction, the instructor and the candidate) appeared together before the assembly.</p>
 
 <p>   'Let them not appear together. Let the instructor come first and proclaim the following <i>ñ</i>atti before the Sa<i>m</i>gha: "Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, hear me. N. N. desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable N. N.; he has been instructed by me. If the Sa<i>m</i>gha is ready, let N. N. come." Then let him be told: "Come on." Let him be told to adjust his upper robe (&amp;c., see chap. 29. 2 ), to raise his joined hands, and to ask (the Sa<i>m</i>gha) for the upasampadâ ordination (by saying), 
 
 <!------------------------page 233------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_233"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 233</font></a>
 
 "I ask the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, for the upasampadâ ordination; might the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, draw me out (of the sinful world) out of compassion towards me. And for the second time, reverend Sirs, I ask, &amp;c. And for the third time, reverend Sirs, I ask, &amp;c."</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:9"></a><font color="GREEN">9</font>. 'Then let a learned, competent Bhikkhu proclaim the following <i>ñ</i>atti before the Sa<i>m</i>gha: "Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, hear me. This person N. N. desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable N. N. If the Sa<i>m</i>gha is ready, let me ask N. N. about the Disqualifications.</p>
 
 <p>   '"Do you hear, N. N.? This is the time for you (&amp;c., see § 7, down to:) you ought to answer: 'It is not.'"</p>
 
 <p>   '"Are you afflicted with the following diseases, &amp;c.?"</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="76:10"></a><font color="GREEN">10</font>. 'Then let a learned, competent Bhikkhu proclaim the following <i>ñ</i>atti before the Sa<i>m</i>gha: "Let the Sa<i>m</i>gha, reverend Sirs, hear me. This person N. N. desires to receive the upasampadâ ordination from the venerable N. N.; he is free from the Disqualifications; his alms-bowl and robes are in due state. N. N. asks the Sa<i>m</i>gha for the upasampadâ ordination with N. N. as upa<i>ggh</i>âya. If the Sa<i>m</i>gha is ready, &amp;c.<a name="page_233_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_233_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>"'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the regulations for the upasampadâ ordination<a name="page_233_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_233_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 234------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_234"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 234</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <!--======================chapter 77======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="77"></a><font color="GREEN">77</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   'Then let them measure the shadow, tell (the newly-ordained Bhikkhu) what season and what date it is, tell him what part of the day it is, tell him the whole formula<a name="page_234_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_234_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, and tell him the four Resources: "The religious life has the morsels of food given in alms for its resource (&amp;c., as in chap. 30. 4)."'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the four Resources.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 78======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="78"></a><font color="GREEN">78</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="78:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time the Bhikkhus, after having conferred the upasampadâ ordination on a certain Bhikkhu, left him alone and went away. Afterwards, as he went alone (to the Ârâma), he met on the way his former wife. She said to him: 'Have you now embraced the religious life?' (He replied): 'Yes, I have embraced the religious life.' 'It is difficult to persons who have embraced religious life, to obtain sexual intercourse; come, let us have intercourse.' He practised intercourse with her, and, in consequence, came late (to the Arâma). The Bhikkhus said: 'How is it, friend, that you are so late?'</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="78:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. Then that Bhikkhu told the whole matter to the Bhikkhus. The Bhikkhus told it to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------page 235------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_235"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 235</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p>   'I prescribe, O Bhikkhus, that you give a companion to a newly-ordained Bhikkhu, and that you tell him the four Interdictions:</p>
 
 <p>   '"A Bhikkhu who has received the upasampadâ ordination ought to abstain from all sexual intercourse even with an animal. A Bhikkhu who practises sexual intercourse is no Sama<i>n</i>a and no follower of the Sakyaputta. As a man whose head is cut off, cannot live any longer with his trunk alone, thus a Bhikkhu who practises sexual intercourse is no Sama<i>n</i>a and no follower of the Sakyaputta. Abstain from doing so as long as your life lasts.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="78:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. '"A Bhikkhu who has received the upasampadâ ordination, ought to abstain from taking what is not given to him, and from theft, even of a blade of grass. A Bhikkhu who takes what is not given to him, or steals it, if it is a pâda (i.e. a quarter of a kârshâpa<i>n</i>a), or of the value of a pâda or worth more than a pâda, is no Sama<i>n</i>a and no follower of the Sakyaputta. As a sear leaf loosed from its stalk cannot become green again, thus a Bhikkhu who takes, &amp;c. Abstain from doing so as long as your life lasts.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="78:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. '"A Bhikkhu who has received the upasampadâ ordination, ought not intentionally to destroy the life of any being down to a worm or an ant. A Bhikkhu who intentionally kills a human being, down to procuring abortion, is no Sama<i>n</i>a and no follower of the Sakyaputta. As a great stone which is broken in two, cannot be reunited, thus a Bhikkhu who intentionally, &amp;c. Abstain from doing so as long as your life lasts.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="78:5"></a><font color="GREEN">5</font>. '"A Bhikkhu who has received the upasampadâ ordination, ought not to attribute to 
 
 <!------------------------page 236------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_236"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 236</font></a>
 
 himself any superhuman condition, and not to say even: 'I find delight in sojourning in an empty place.' A Bhikkhu who with bad intention and out of covetousness attributes to himself a superhuman condition, which he has not, and which he is not possessed of, a state of <i>gh</i>âna (mystic meditation), or one of the vimokkhas<a name="page_236_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_236_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>, or one of the samâdhis (states of self-concentration), or one of the samâpattis (the attainment of the four <i>gh</i>ânas and four of the eight vimokkhas), or one of the Paths (of sanctification), or one of the Fruits thereof, is no Sama<i>n</i>a and no follower of the Sakyaputta. As a palm tree of which the top sprout has been cut off, cannot grow again, thus a Bhikkhu who with bad intention, &amp;c. Abstain from doing so as long as your life lasts."'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the four Interdicts.</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <!--======================chapter 79======================-->
 
 <h3 align="center"><a name="79"></a><font color="GREEN">79</font>.</h3>
 
 <p>   <a name="79:1"></a><font color="GREEN">1</font>. At that time a certain Bhikkhu against whom expulsion<a name="page_236_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_236_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a> had been pronounced for his refusal to see an offence (committed by himself), returned to
 
 <!------------------------page 237------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_237"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 237</font></a>
 
 the world. Afterwards he came back to the Bhikkhus and asked them for the upasampadâ ordination.</p>
 
 <p>   They told this thing to the Blessed One.</p>
 
 <p>   'In case, O Bhikkhus, that a Bhikkhu against whom expulsion has been pronounced for his refusal to see an offence (committed by himself), returns to the world, and afterwards comes back to the Bhikkhus and asks them for the upasampadâ ordination, let them say to him: "Will you see that offence?" If he replies: "I will see it," let him be admitted to the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination; if he replies: "I will not see it," let him not be admitted to the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="79:2"></a><font color="GREEN">2</font>. 'When he has received the pabba<i>gg</i>â ordination let them say to him: "Will you see that offence?" If he says: "I will see it," let him be admitted to the upasampadâ ordination; if he says: "I will not see it," let him not be admitted to the upasampadâ ordination.</p>
 
 <p>   'When he has received the upasampadâ ordination (&amp;c., as before). If he says: "I will see it," let him be restored<a name="page_237_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_237_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a>; if he says: "I will not see it," let him not be restored.</p>
 
 <p>   'When he has been restored, let them say to him: "Do you see that offence?" If he sees it, well and good; if he does not see it, let them expel him again, if it is possible to bring about unanimity (of the fraternity for the sentence of expulsion); if that is impossible, it is no offence to live and to dwell together (with such a Bhikkhu).</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="79:3"></a><font color="GREEN">3</font>. 'In case, O Bhikkhus, that a Bhikkhu against whom expulsion has been pronounced for his refusal
 
 <!------------------------page 238------------------------>
 
 <a name="page_238"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 238</font></a>
 
 to atone for an offence (committed by himself), &amp;c.<a name="page_238_fr_1"></a><a href="#page_238_note_1"><sup><small>1</small></sup></a> When he has been restored, let them say to him: "Atone now for that offence." If he atones for it, well and good, &amp;c.</p>
 
 <p>   <a name="79:4"></a><font color="GREEN">4</font>. 'In case, O Bhikkhus, that a Bhikkhu against whom expulsion has been pronounced for his refusal to renounce a false doctrine, &amp;c.<a name="page_238_fr_2"></a><a href="#page_238_note_2"><sup><small>2</small></sup></a> When he has been restored, let them say to him: "Renounce now that false doctrine." If he renounces it, well and good, &amp;c.'</p>
 
 <hr width="33%" align="center">
 
 <p align="center">End of the first Khandhaka, which is called the Great Khandhaka<a name="page_238_fr_3"></a><a href="#page_238_note_3"><sup><small>3</small></sup></a>.</p>
 
 <hr>
 
 <p align="center"><a href="sbe13.htm">Next: Mahâvagga -  Second Khandaka</a></p>
 
 <!--======================footnotes======================-->
 
 <hr>
 
 <h3 align="center">Footnotes</h3>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 73------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_73"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 73</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_73_note_1"></a><a href="#page_73_fr_1">1</a> To this book is prefixed, as introduction, an account of the first events after Gotama's attaining Buddhahood, down to the conversion of his two chief disciples, Sâriputta and Moggallâna (chaps. 1-24). Among the elements of historical or legendary character with which, in the Vinaya Pi<i>t</i>aka, the discussion of the monastic discipline is interwoven, this account occupies by far the first place, both in extent and in importance. For it contains the oldest version accessible to us now and, most probably, for ever, of what the Buddhist fraternity deemed to be the history of their Master's life in its most important period.</p>
 
 <p>The connection in which this legendary narration stands with the main subject of the first Khandhaka is not difficult to account for. The regulations regarding the admission to the fraternity, which are discussed in this Khandhaka, could not but present themselves to the redactors of the Pi<i>t</i>aka as being the very basis of their religious discipline and monastic life. It was possible to fancy the existence of the Sa<i>m</i>gha without the Pâtimokkha rules, or without the regulations about the Pavâra<i>n</i>â festival, but it was impossible to realise the idea of a Sa<i>m</i>gha without rules showing who was to be regarded as a duly admitted member of the fraternity, and who was not. It is quite natural, therefore, that the stories or legends concerning the ordination of Bhikkhus were put in connection with the record of the very first events of the history of the Sa<i>m</i>gha. Nor is it difficult to account for the theory formulated by the historians of the Buddhist ecclesiastical law, of different successive forms in which the ordination of Bhikkhus had been performed. In the beginning, of course, there was nobody but the Buddha himself who could ordain Bhikkhus; to him those who desired to be received, expressed their wish, and he conferred on them the pabba<i>gg</i>â and upasampadâ ordinations by the formula: 'Ehi bhikkhu,' &amp;c. (see I, 6, 32, 34, &amp;c.) It was a very natural conception that afterwards, as the Sa<i>m</i>gha grew larger, the Buddha should have transferred the power of admitting new members to the Bhikkhus themselves, and should have instituted that form of ordination which the redactors of the Pi<i>t</i>aka found valid at their own time.</p>
 
 <p>The transition, however, from the supposed oldest form of ordination (the so-called ehi-bhikkhu-upasampadâ) to that latter form is in the Vinaya legends not represented as immediate. There is described an intermediate stage between the two, the ordination by the three sara<i>n</i>agamanas, or by the candidate's three times repeated declaration of his taking refuge in the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Sa<i>m</i>gha (see Mahâvagga I, 12). The reason which has led the redactors of the Vinaya Pi<i>t</i>aka to this construction, was most probably the important part which in the upasampadâ service of the later time devolved upon the preceptor (upa<i>ggh</i>âya) of the candidate. As only learned Bhikkhus, who had completed the tenth year after their own upasampadâ, could perform the function of upa<i>ggh</i>âya at the upasampadâ ordination of other Bhikkhus (Mahâvagga I, 31, 8), it was natural that the redactors of the Vinaya found it impossible to ascribe this form of upasampadâ service to the first times of Buddha's teaching. For these times, therefore, they recorded another form, the upasampadâ by the three sara<i>n</i>agamanas, the introduction of which they assigned, very naturally, to the time soon after the conversion of Yasa's friends, by which event the number of Bhikkhus had been augmented at once from seven to sixty-one.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 74------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_74"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 74</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_74_note_1"></a><a href="#page_74_fr_1">1</a> The Lilayan or Phalgu river in Behar; see General Cunningham's map, Archaeological Reports, vol. i. plate iii.</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_74_note_2"></a><a href="#page_74_fr_2">2</a> After having reached the sambodhi and before preaching to the world the truth he has acquired, the Buddha remains, according to the tradition, during some weeks at Uruvelâ, 'enjoying the bliss of emancipation.' The Mahâvagga, which contains these legends in their oldest forms, assigns to this stay a period of four times seven days; the later tradition is unanimous in extending it to seven times seven days (Buddhaghosa in the commentary on the Mahâvagga; <i>G</i>âtaka Atthav. vol. i. p. 77 seq.; Dîpava<i>m</i>sa I, 29, 30; Lalita Vistara, p. 488 seq.; Beal, Romantic Legend, p. 236 seq., &amp;c.)</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 75------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_75"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 75</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_75_note_1"></a><a href="#page_75_fr_1">1</a> The Chain of Causation, or the doctrine of the twelve nidânas (causes of existence), contains, as has often been observed, in a more developed form an answer to the same problem to which the second and third of the four Noble Truths (ariyasa<i>kk</i>a) also try to give a solution, viz. the problem of the origin and destruction of suffering. The Noble Truths simply reduce the origin of suffering to Thirst, or Desire (Ta<i>n</i>hâ), in its threefold form, thirst for pleasure, thirst for existence, thirst for prosperity (see I, 6, 20). In the system of the twelve nidânas Thirst also has found its place among the causes of suffering, but it is not considered as the immediate cause. A concatenation of other categories is inserted between to<i>n</i>hâ and its ultimate effect; and on the other hand, the investigation of causes is carried on further beyond to<i>n</i>hâ. The question is here asked, What does to<i>n</i>hâ come from? and thus the series of causes and effects is led back to aviggâ (Ignorance), as its deepest root. We may add that the redactors of the Pi<i>t</i>akas, who of course could not but observe this parallelity between the second and third ariyasa<i>kk</i>as and the system of the twelve nidânas, go so far, in one instance (A<u>n</u>guttara-Nikâya, Tika-Nipâta, fol. <i>k</i>e of the Phayre MS.), as to directly replace, in giving the text of the four ariyasa<i>kk</i>as, the second and third of them by the twelve nidânas, in direct and reverse order respectively. Professor Childers has furnished a valuable note on the nidânas; see Colebrooke, Miscellaneous Essays (second edition), II, 453 seq.</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_75_note_2"></a><a href="#page_75_fr_2">2</a> In the Sammâdi<i>tth</i>isuttanta (Ma<i>ggh</i>ima-Nikâya, fol. khû of Turnour's MS.) we find the following explanation of what Ignorance is: 'Not to know Suffering, not to know the Cause of suffering, not to know the Cessation of suffering, not to know the Path which leads to the cessation of suffering, this is called Ignorance.' The same is repeated in the explanation of the nidâna formula, which is given in the Vibha<u>n</u>ga (Abhidhamma-Pi<i>t</i>aka, Pa<i>t</i>i<i>kk</i>asamuppâda-vibha<u>n</u>ga, fol. <i>k</i>i of the Phayre MS.), and we must accept it, therefore, as the authentic expression of Buddhistical belief. It is obvious, however, that this explanation leaves room for another question. Ignorance, we are told, is the source of all evil and of all suffering, and the subject ignored is stated to be the four Truths. But who is the subject that ignores them? All attributes (as the vi<i>ññ</i>â<i>n</i>a, &amp;c.), that constitute sentient beings and enable them to know or to ignore, are said to be first produced by Ignorance, and we shou1d conclude, therefore, that they cannot exist before Ignorance has begun to act. Or are we to understand that it is the Ignorance incurred by a sentient being in a preceding existence, that causes the sa<i>m</i>khâras and Consciousness, the connecting links between the different existences, to act and to bring about the birth of a new being?</p>
 
 <p>As is well known, this Ignorance (Avidyâ) plays a great part also in the Brahmanical philosophy of the Upanishads; and the Buddhist belief is, no doubt, founded to a considerable extent on older theories. But we cannot venture in a note to touch upon one of the most difficult and interesting questions which await the research of Indianists.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 76------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_76"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 76</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_76_note_1"></a><a href="#page_76_fr_1">1</a> It is very frequently stated that there are three sa<i>m</i>khâras or productions: kâyasa<i>m</i>khâra, va<i>k</i>isa<i>m</i>khâra, and <i>k</i>ittasa<i>m</i>khâra, or, productions of body, of speech, and of thought (see, for instance, the Sammâdi<i>tth</i>isuttanta, Ma<i>ggh</i>ima-Nikâya, fol. khû of Turnour's MS.) The kâyasa<i>m</i>khâra consists, according to the Sa<i>m</i>khâra-Yamaka (Abhidhamma-Pi<i>t</i>aka), in inhalation and expiration (assâsapassâsâ); the va<i>k</i>îsa<i>m</i>khâra in attention and investigation (vitakkavi<i>k</i>ârâ); the <i>k</i>ittasa<i>m</i>khâra in ideas, sensations, and all attributes of mind except attention and investigation (sa<i>ññ</i>â <i>k</i>a vedanâ <i>k</i>a <i>th</i>apetvâ vitakkavi<i>k</i>âre sabbe pi <i>k</i>ittasampayuttakâ dhammâ). The Vibha<u>n</u>ga (Abhidhamma-Pi<i>t</i>aka, Pa<i>t</i>i<i>kk</i>asamuppâdavibha<u>n</u>ga, I.I.{sic. ?}) gives, when discussing the sa<i>m</i>khâras, six categories instead of the three: 'Now which are the sa<i>m</i>khâras that are produced by Ignorance? Sa<i>m</i>khâras (or, productions) that lead to righteousness, sa<i>m</i>khâras that lead to sinfulness, sa<i>m</i>khâras that lead to immovability, productions of body, of speech, and of thought.' The Pâli words are: 'Tattha katame avi<i>gg</i>âpa<i>kk</i>ayâ sa<i>m</i>khârâ? pu<i>ññ</i>âbhisa<i>m</i>khâro apu<i>ññ</i>âbhisa<i>m</i>khâro â<i>n</i>a<i>ñg</i>âbhisa<i>m</i>khâro kâyasa<i>m</i>khâro va<i>k</i>isa<i>m</i>khâro <i>k</i>ittasa<i>m</i>khâro.' The list of fifty-five categories belonging to the sa<i>m</i>khâra-khandha, which Sp. Hardy gives in his Manual (p. 404 seq.; comp. also Rh. D., 'Buddhism,' p. 91 seq., and 'Buddhist Suttas from the Pâli,' <a href="../sbe11/sbe1108.htm#page_242">p. 242</a>), is not founded, as far as we know, on the authority of the Pi<i>t</i>akas themselves, but on later compendia and commentaries.</p>

 <a name="footnotes_page_77"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 77</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_77_note_1"></a><a href="#page_77_fr_1">1</a> I.e. eye, ear, nose, tongue, body (or the faculty of touch), and mind.</p>

 <!------------------------footnotes page 79------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_79"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 79</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_79_note_1"></a><a href="#page_79_fr_1">1</a> Buddhaghosa: 'The goat-herds used to go to the shadow of that banyan tree and to sit there; therefore it was called the banyan tree of the goat-herds.' The northern Buddhists say that this tree had been planted by a shepherd boy, during the Bodhisatta's six years' penance, in order to shelter him; see Beal, Rom. Legend, pp. 192, 238, and the Mahâvastu.</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_79_note_2"></a><a href="#page_79_fr_2">2</a> 'Huhu<u>n</u>ka<i>g</i>âtiko.' Buddhaghosa: 'Because he was di<i>tth</i>ama<u>n</u>galika, he became filled with haughtiness and wrath, and went about uttering the sound "huhu<i>m</i>."' Di<i>tth</i>ama<u>n</u>galika (having seen something auspicious ?) is obscure to us.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 81------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_81"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 81</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_81_note_1"></a><a href="#page_81_fr_1">1</a> Buddhaghosa says that Râ<i>g</i>âyatana (lit. a royal apartment) was the name of a tree. It is the same tree which in the Lalita Vistara (p. 493, ed. Calcutta) is called Târâya<i>n</i>a, and in the Dipava<i>m</i>sa (II, 50) Khîrapâla. The place where the two merchants met Buddha, is thus described in the Mahâvastu: kshîri-kâvanasha<i>nd</i>e bahudevatake <i>k</i>etiye.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 82------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_82"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 82</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_82_note_1"></a><a href="#page_82_fr_1">1</a> The term Tathâgata is, in the Buddhistical literature, exclusively applied to Sammâsambuddhas, and it is more especially used in the Pi<i>t</i>akas when the Buddha is represented as speaking of himself in the third person as 'the Tathâgata.' The meaning 'sentient being,' which is given to the word in the Abhidhânappadîpikâ, and in Childers's Dictionary, is not confirmed, as far as we know, by any passage of the Pi<i>t</i>akas. This translation of the word is very possibly based merely on a misunderstanding of the phrase often repeated in the Sutta Pi<i>t</i>aka: hoti tathâgato para<i>m</i> mara<i>n</i>â, which means, of course, 'does a Buddha exist after death?' In the <i>G</i>aina books we sometimes find the term tatthagaya (tatragata), 'he who has attained that world, i.e. emancipation,' applied to the <i>G</i>inas as opposed to other beings who are called ihagaya (idhagata), 'living in this world.' See, for instance, the <i>G</i>ina<i>k</i>aritra, § 16. Considering the close relation in which most of the dogmatical terms of the <i>G</i>ainas stand to those of the Bauddhas, it is difficult to believe that tathâgata and tatthagaya should not originally have conveyed very similar ideas. We think that on the long way from the original Mâgadhî to the Pâli and Sanskrit, the term tatthagata or tatthâgata (tatra + âgata), 'he who has arrived there, i.e. at emancipation,' may very easily have undergone the change into tathâgata, which would have made it unintelligible, were we not able to compare its unaltered form as preserved by the <i>G</i>ainas.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 83------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_83"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 83</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_83_note_1"></a><a href="#page_83_fr_1">1</a> The four guardian gods of the quarters of the world; see Hardy's Manual, p. 24. Their Pâli names, as given in the Abhidhânappadîpikâ, vv. 31, 32, the Dîpava<i>m</i>sa XVI, 12, &amp;c., were, Dhatara<i>tth</i>a, Virû<i>Ih</i>aka, Virûpakkha, and Vessava<i>n</i>a or Kuvera.</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_83_note_2"></a><a href="#page_83_fr_2">2</a> Onîtapattapâ<i>n</i>i, which is said very frequently of a person who has finished his meal, is translated by Childers, 'whose hand is removed from the bowl' (comp. also Trenckner, Pali Miscellany, p. 66). We do not think this explanation right, though it agrees with, or probably is based on, a note of Buddhaghosa ('pattato <i>k</i>a apanîtapâ<i>n</i>i<i>m</i>'). Onîta, i.e. avanita, is not apanîta, and the end of the dinner was marked, not by the Bhikkhu's removing his hand from the bowl, but by his washing the bowl (see <i>K</i>ullavagga VIII, 4, 6), and, of course, his hands. In Sanskrit the meaning of ava-nî is, to pour (water) upon something; see the Petershurg Dictionary. We have translated, therefore, onîtapattapâ<i>n</i>i accordingly.</p>

 <!------------------------footnotes page 84------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_84"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 84</font></a>

 <p><a name="page_84_note_1"></a><a href="#page_84_fr_1">1</a> Because there was no Sa<i>m</i>gha at that time, their declaration of taking refuge, by which they became upâsakas, could refer only to the dyad (the Buddha and the Dhamma), instead of to the triad of the Buddha, the Dhamma, and the Sa<i>m</i>gha.</p>

 <!------------------------footnotes page 85------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_85"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 85</font></a>

 <p><a name="page_85_note_1"></a><a href="#page_85_fr_1">1</a> The upadhis (substrata of existence) are specified in the commentary on the Sutta-Nipâta, ap. Dhammapada, p. 433: 'sabbûpadhina<i>m</i> parikkhayâ 'ti sabbesa<i>m</i> khandhakâmagu<i>n</i>akilesâbhisa<i>m</i>khârabhedâna<i>m</i> upadhîna<i>m</i> parikkhî<i>n</i>attâ.' Probably abhisa<i>m</i>khâra is not co-ordinate with the other members of the compound, but is determined by them, comp. pabba<i>gg</i>âbhisa<i>m</i>khâra, iddhâbhisa<i>m</i>khâra, gamikâbhisa<i>m</i>khâra. The upadhis, therefore, according to this passage, consist: firstly, in the actions of mind that are directed towards the khandhas (i.e. that have the effect of propagating and augmenting the dominion of the khandhas); secondly, in the actions tending to the fivefold pleasures of sense; and thirdly, in those connected with kilesa (evil passion).</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_85_note_2"></a><a href="#page_85_fr_2">2</a> Buddhaghosa explains ana<i>kkh</i>ariya by anua<i>kkh</i>ariya, which is alike unintelligible to us. The Lalita Vistara (p. 515, ed. Calcutta) has abhîksh<i>n</i>am ('repeatedly').</p>

 <!------------------------footnotes page 97------------------------>

 <!------------------------footnotes page 98------------------------>

 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 99------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_99"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 99</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_99_note_1"></a><a href="#page_99_fr_1">1</a> Those three Bhikkhus of the five, who had been converted, went about for alms; while the Buddha remained with their two companions, and instructed them.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 100------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_100"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 100</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_100_note_1"></a><a href="#page_100_fr_1">1</a> This is shown exactly in the same way and with the same words that are used in § 38 with regard to the body. Body, sensations, perceptions, sa<i>m</i>khâras, and consciousness are the well-known five classes (khandha) of bodily and mental parts and powers; see Rh. D., 'Buddhism,' p. 90 seq. The self (attâ), which, if it exists at all, must be permanent and imperishable, is not to be found in any one of these five classes, which are all subject to origin and decay. This discourse of the Buddha's, which is frequently called the Anattalakkha<i>n</i>a Sutta (Sutta of the not having the signs of self), shows the perishable nature of the five khandhas, and that the khandhas are not the self. But it does not deal with the question, whether the self exists or not, in any other way.</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_100_note_2"></a><a href="#page_100_fr_2">2</a> See the note on chap. 1. 2.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 101------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_101"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 101</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_101_note_1"></a><a href="#page_101_fr_1">1</a> Here follow the same questions, answers, and rejoinders, with regard to sensation, perception, the sa<i>m</i>khâras, and consciousness.</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_101_note_2"></a><a href="#page_101_fr_2">2</a> The same with regard to the other four khandhas.</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_101_note_3"></a><a href="#page_101_fr_3">3</a> Compare Burnouf, 'Lotus de la bonne Loi,' p. 481.</p>
 
 <p>
 
 <!------------------------footnotes page 102------------------------>
 
 <a name="footnotes_page_102"><font size="1" color="GREEN">p. 102</font></a>
 
 </p>
 
 <p><a name="page_102_note_1"></a><a href="#page_102_fr_1">1</a> See the note on § 9.</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_102_note_2"></a><a href="#page_102_fr_2">2</a> A well-known scene in the life of the Bodhisatta has evidently been represented after the model of this story. See <i>G</i>âtaka I, p. 61; Lalita Vistara, p. 251; Bigandet, Life of Gaudama, p. 55. Nowhere in the Pâli Pi<i>t</i>akas is the story told about the Bodhisatta himself.</p>
 
 <p><a name="page_102_note_3"></a><a href="#page_102_fr_3">3</a> This was a position of honour among the merchants. In the later literature we hear of an office of se<i>tth</i>i (se<i>tth</i>i-<i>tth</i>âna) in a city, to which any one with the requisite wealth and talent was eligible (<i>G</i>âtaka I, 120-122); and, according to the Mahâva<i>m</i>sa, the king appointed to an office called se<i>tth</i>itâ, apparently at his court (Mah. p. 69). The Gahapati, or Treasurer, one of the seven jewels of a king, is explained by Buddhaghosa to be se<i>tth</i>i-gahapati (see Rh. D.'s note on Mahâ-sudassana Sutta I, 41). 'The Se<i>tth</i>i,' standing alone, or 'the Mahâ-se<i>tth</i>i,' means Anâtha Pi<i>nd</i>ika (<i>G</i>âtaka I, 95, 227-230; Dhammapada Commentary, p. 395). Below, in chapter 9, § 1, it would seem that the rank of se<i>tth</i>i was hereditary, and this is confirmed by the later literature; but this applies to the social rank only, and not to the office.</p>
 
 <p>
